<th scope="row">\n         <a href="/wiki/Geographic_Names_Information_System" title="Geographic Names Information System">\n          GNIS\n         </a>\n         feature ID\n        </th>\n        <td>\n         1499957\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GR3_4-0">\n          <a href="#cite_note-GR3-4">\n           [4]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr class="mergedtoprow">\n        <th scope="row">\n         Website\n        </th>\n        <td>\n         <a class="external text" href="http://www.ci.richmond.va.us/" rel="nofollow">\n <span style="font-size:87%;">\n           <b>\n            Nomenclature evolution\n           </b>\n          </span>\n         </center>\n         Prior to 1071 \xe2\x80\x93\n         <a class="external text" href="http://www.lion1906.com/departements/seine-maritime/richemont-.pdf" rel="nofollow">\n          Richemont\n         </a>\n         : a town in Normandy, France.\n         <br/>\n         1071 to 1501 \xe2\x80\x93\n         <a href="/wiki/Richmond,_North_Yorkshire" title="Richmond, North Yorkshire">\n          Richmond\n         </a>\n         : a castle town in Yorkshire, UK.\n         <br/>\n         1501 to 1742 \xe2\x80\x93\n         <a href="/wiki/Richmond,_London" title="Richmond, London">\n          Richmond\n         </a>\n         , a palace town in Surrey, UK.\n         <br/>\n         1742 to present \xe2\x80\x93 Richmond, Virginia.\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <p>\n       <b>\n        Richmond\n       </b>\n       (\n       <span class="nowrap">\n        <span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt">\n         <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">\n          /\n          <span style="border-bottom:1px dotted">\n           <span title="/\xcb\x88/: primary stress follows">\n            \xcb\x88\n           </span>\n           <span title="\'r\' in \'rye\'">\n            r\n           </span>\n           <span title="/\xc9\xaa/: \'i\' in \'kit\'">\n            \xc9\xaa\n           </span>\n           <span title="/t\xca\x83/: \'ch\' in \'China\'">\n            t\xca\x83\n           </span>\n           <span title="\'m\' in \'my\'">\n            m\n           </span>\n           <span title="/\xc9\x99n/: \'on\' in \'button\'">\n            \xc9\x99n\n           </span>\n           <span title="\'d\' in \'dye\'">\n            d\n           </span>\n          </span>\n          /\n         </a>\n        </span>\n       </span>\n       <a href="/wiki/Help:Pronunciation_respelling_key" title="Help:Pronunciation respelling key">\n        <small title="English pronunciation respelling">\n         <i>\n          <b>\n           RICH\n          </b>\n          -m\xc9\x99nd\n         </i>\n        </small>\n       </a>\n       ) is the capital of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_(U.S._state)" title="Commonwealth (U.S. state)">\n        Commonwealth\n       </a>\n       of\n       <a href="/wiki/Virginia" title="Virginia">\n        Virginia\n       </a>\n       . It is the center of the Richmond\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Metropolitan_Statistical_Area" title="Metropolitan Statistical Area">\n        Metropolitan Statistical Area\n       </a>\n       (MSA) and the\n       <a href="/wiki/Greater_Richmond_Region" title="Greater Richmond Region">\n        Greater Richmond Region\n       </a>\n       . It was incorporated in 1742, and has been an\n       <a href="/wiki/Independent_city_(United_States)" title="Independent city (United States)">\n        independent city\n       </a>\n       since 1871.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       As of the\n       <a href="/wiki/2010_United_States_Census" title="2010 United States Census">\n        2010 census\n       </a>\n       , the population was 204,214;\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-QF_5-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-QF-5">\n         [5]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       in 2016, the population was estimated to be 223,170,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-QF_5-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-QF-5">\n         [5]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       the\n       <a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_in_Virginia" title="List of cities in Virginia">\n        fourth-most populous city in Virginia\n       </a>\n       . The\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Richmond-Petersburg" title="Richmond-Petersburg">\n        Richmond Metropolitan Area\n       </a>\n       has a population of 1,260,029, the\n       <a href="/wiki/Virginia_statistical_areas" title="Virginia statistical areas">\n        third-most populous metro in the state\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Richmond is located at the\n       <a href="/wiki/Fall_line" title="Fall line">\n        fall line\n       </a>\n       of the\n       <a href="/wiki/James_River" title="James River">\n        James River\n       </a>\n       , 44 miles (71\xc2\xa0km) west of\n       <a href="/wiki/Williamsburg,_Virginia" title="Williamsburg, Virginia">\n        Williamsburg\n       </a>\n       , 66 miles (106\xc2\xa0km) east of\n       <a href="/wiki/Charlottesville,_Virginia" title="Charlottesville, Virginia">\n        Charlottesville\n       </a>\n       , and 98 miles (158\xc2\xa0km) south of\n       <a href="/wiki/Washington,_D.C." title="Washington, D.C.">\n        Washington, D.C.\n       </a>\n       Surrounded by\n       <a href="/wiki/Henrico_County,_Virginia" title="Henrico County, Virginia">\n        Henrico\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Chesterfield_County,_Virginia" title="Chesterfield County, Virginia">\n        Chesterfield\n       </a>\n       counties, the city is located at the intersections of\n       <a href="/wiki/Interstate_95_in_Virginia" title="Interstate 95 in Virginia">\n        Interstate 95\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Interstate_64_in_Virginia" title="Interstate 64 in Virginia">\n        Interstate 64\n       </a>\n       , and encircled by\n       <a href="/wiki/Interstate_295_(Virginia)" title="Interstate 295 (Virginia)">\n        Interstate 295\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Virginia_State_Route_288" title="Virginia State Route 288">\n        Virginia State Route 288\n       </a>\n       . Major suburbs include\n       <a href="/wiki/Midlothian,_Virginia" title="Midlothian, Virginia">\n        Midlothian\n       </a>\n       to the southwest,\n       <a href="/wiki/Glen_Allen,_Virginia" title="Glen Allen, Virginia">\n        Glen Allen\n       </a>\n       to the north and west,\n       <a href="/wiki/Short_Pump,_Virginia" title="Short Pump, Virginia">\n        Short Pump\n       </a>\n       to the west and\n       <a href="/wiki/Mechanicsville,_Virginia" title="Mechanicsville, Virginia">\n        Mechanicsville\n       </a>\n       to the northeast.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The site of Richmond had been an important village of the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Powhatan_Confederacy" title="Powhatan Confederacy">\n        Powhatan Confederacy\n       </a>\n       , and was briefly settled by English colonists from\n       <a href="/wiki/Jamestown,_Virginia" title="Jamestown, Virginia">\n        Jamestown\n       </a>\n       in 1609, and in 1610\xe2\x80\x931611. The present city of Richmond was founded in 1737. It became the capital of the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Colony_and_Dominion_of_Virginia" title="Colony and Dominion of Virginia">\n        Colony and Dominion of Virginia\n       </a>\n       in 1780, replacing\n       <a href="/wiki/Williamsburg,_Virginia" title="Williamsburg, Virginia">\n        Williamsburg\n       </a>\n       . During the\n       <a href="/wiki/American_Revolution" title="American Revolution">\n        Revolutionary War\n       </a>\n       period, several notable events occurred in the city, including\n       <a href="/wiki/Patrick_Henry" title="Patrick Henry">\n        Patrick Henry\n       </a>\n       \'s "\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Give_me_liberty_or_give_me_death" title="Give me liberty or give me death">\n        Give me liberty or give me death\n       </a>\n       " speech in 1775 at\n       <a href="/wiki/St._John%27s_Episcopal_Church_(Richmond,_Virginia)" title="St. John\'s Episcopal Church (Richmond, Virginia)">\n        St. John\'s Church\n       </a>\n       , and the passage of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Statute_for_Religious_Freedom" title="Virginia Statute for Religious Freedom">\n        Virginia Statute for Religious Freedom\n       </a>\n       written by\n       <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Jefferson" title="Thomas Jefferson">\n        Thomas Jefferson\n       </a>\n       . During the\n       <a href="/wiki/American_Civil_War" title="American Civil War">\n        American Civil War\n       </a>\n       , Richmond served as the second and permanent capital of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Confederate_States_of_America" title="Confederate States of America">\n        Confederate States of America\n       </a>\n       . The city entered the 20th century with one of the world\'s first successful electric\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Streetcar" title="Streetcar">\n        streetcar\n       </a>\n       systems. The\n       <a href="/wiki/Jackson_Ward" title="Jackson Ward">\n        Jackson Ward\n       </a>\n       neighborhood is a national hub of African-American commerce and culture.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Richmond\'s economy is primarily driven by law, finance, and government, with federal, state, and local governmental agencies, as well as notable legal and banking firms, located in the downtown area. The city is home to both the\n       <a href="/wiki/United_States_Court_of_Appeals_for_the_Fourth_Circuit" title="United States Court of Appeals for the Fourth Circuit">\n        United States Court of Appeals for the Fourth Circuit\n       </a>\n       , one of 13\n       <a href="/wiki/United_States_courts_of_appeals" title="United States courts of appeals">\n        United States courts of appeals\n       </a>\n       , and the\n       <a href="/wiki/Federal_Reserve_Bank_of_Richmond" title="Federal Reserve Bank of Richmond">\n        Federal Reserve Bank of Richmond\n       </a>\n       , one of 12\n       <a href="/wiki/Federal_Reserve_System" title="Federal Reserve System">\n        Federal Reserve Banks\n       </a>\n       .\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dominion_Resources" title="Dominion Resources">\n        Dominion Resources\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/WestRock" title="WestRock">\n        WestRock\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Fortune_500" title="Fortune 500">\n        Fortune 500\n       </a>\n       companies, are headquartered in the city, with others in the metropolitan area.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fortune500_6-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Fortune500-6">\n         [6]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n      </p>\n      <div class="toc"          <span class="toctext">\n             Food\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n         </ul>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-26">\n         <a href="#Parks_and_outdoor_recreation">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           6\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Parks and outdoor recreation\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-27">\n         <a href="#Sports">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           7\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Sports\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-28">\n         <a href="#Media">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           8\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Media\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-29">\n         <a href="#Government_and_politics">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           9\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Government and politics\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-30">\n         <a href="#Education">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           10\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Education\n          </span>\n         </a>\n         <ul>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-31">\n           <a href="#Colleges_and_universities">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             10.1\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Colleges and universities\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n         </ul>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-32">\n         <a href="#Infrastructure">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           11\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Infrastructure\n          </span>\n         </a>\n         <ul>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-33">\n           <a href="#Transportation">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             11.1\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Transportation\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-34">\n           <a href="#Major_highways">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             11.2\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Major highways\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-35">\n           <a href="#Utilities">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             11.3\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Utilities\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n         </ul>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-36">\n         <a href="#International_relations">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           12\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           International relations\n          </span>\n         </a>\n         <ul>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-37">\n           <a href="#Sister_cities">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             12.1\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Sister cities\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n         </ul>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-38">\n         <a href="#See_also">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           13\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           See also\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-39">\n         <a href="#Notes">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           14\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Notes\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-40">\n         <a href="#References">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           15\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           References\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-41">\n         <a href="#Further_reading">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           16\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Further reading\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-42">\n         <a href="#External_links">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           17\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           External links\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n       </ul>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="History">\n        History\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Richmond,_Virginia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main articles:\n       <a href="/wiki/History_of_Richmond,_Virginia" title="History of Richmond, Virginia">\n        History of Richmond, Virginia\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_Richmond,_Virginia" title="Timeline of Richmond, Virginia">\n        Timeline of Richmond, Virginia\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       See also:\n       <a href="/wiki/Richmond_in_the_American_Civil_War" title="Richmond in the American Civil War">\n        Richmond in the American Civil War\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Colonial_era">\n        Colonial era\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Richmond,_Virginia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Colonial era">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       After the first permanent English-speaking settlement was established in April 1607, at\n       <a href="/wiki/Jamestown,_Virginia" title="Jamestown, Virginia">\n        Jamestown, Virginia\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Newport" title="Christopher Newport">\n        Captain Christopher Newport\n       </a>\n       led explorers northwest up the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/James_River_(Virginia)" title="James River (Virginia)">\n        James River\n       </a>\n       , to an area that was inhabited by\n       <a href="/wiki/Powhatan" title="Powhatan">\n        Powhatan\n       </a>\n       Native Americans.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7">\n        <a href="#cite_note-7">\n         [7]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In 1737, planter\n       <a href="/wiki/William_Byrd_II" title="William Byrd II">\n        William Byrd II\n       </a>\n       commissioned\n       <a href="/wiki/William_Mayo_(civil_engineer)" title="William Mayo (civil engineer)">\n        Major William Mayo\n       </a>\n       to lay out the original town grid. Byrd named the city "Richmond" after the English town of\n       <a href="/wiki/Richmond,_London" title="Richmond, London">\n        Richmond\n       </a>\n       near (and now part of) London, because the view of the James River was strikingly similar to the view of the\n       <a href="/wiki/River_Thames" title="River Thames">\n        River Thames\n       </a>\n       from\n       <a href="/wiki/Richmond_Hill,_London" title="Richmond Hill, London">\n        Richmond Hill\n       </a>\n       in England, where he had spent time during his youth. The settlement was laid out in April 1737, and was incorporated as a town in 1742.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8">\n        <a href="#cite_note-8">\n         [8]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Revolution">\n        Revolution\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Richmond,_Virginia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Revolution">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Patrick_Henry_Rothermel.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="750" data-file-width="580" height="284" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Patrick_Henry_Rothermel.jpg/220px-Patrick_Henry_Rothermel.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Patrick_Henry_Rothermel.jpg/330px-Patrick_Henry_Rothermel.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Patrick_Henry_Rothermel.jpg/440px-Patrick_Henry_Rothermel.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Patrick_Henry_Rothermel.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <a href="/wiki/Patrick_Henry" title="Patrick Henry">\n          Patrick Henry\n         </a>\n         delivered his "Liberty or Death" speech at\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saint_John%27s_Church,_Richmond,_Virginia" title="Saint John\'s Church, Richmond, Virginia">\n          St. John\'s Church\n         </a>\n         in Richmond, helping to ignite the American Revolution\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       In 1775,\n       <a href="/wiki/Patrick_Henry" title="Patrick Henry">\n        Patrick Henry\n       </a>\n       delivered his famous "\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Give_me_Liberty_or_Give_me_Death" title="Give me Liberty or Give me Death">\n        Give me Liberty or Give me Death\n       </a>\n       " speech in\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saint_John%27s_Church,_Richmond,_Virginia" title="Saint John\'s Church, Richmond, Virginia">\n        St. John\'s Church\n       </a>\n       in Richmond, crucial for deciding Virginia\'s participation in the\n       <a href="/wiki/First_Continental_Congress" title="First Continental Congress">\n        First Continental Congress\n       </a>\n       and setting the course for revolution and independence.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-liberty_death_9-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-liberty_death-9">\n         [9]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       On April 18, 1780, the state capital was moved from the colonial capital of\n       <a href="/wiki/Williamsburg,_Virginia" title="Williamsburg, Virginia">\n        Williamsburg\n       </a>\n       to Richmond, to provide a more centralized location for Virginia\'s increasing westerly population, as well as to isolate the capital from British attack.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-VHS_10-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-VHS-10">\n         [10]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The latter motive proved to be in vain, and in 1781, under the command of\n       <a href="/wiki/Benedict_Arnold" title="Benedict Arnold">\n        Benedict Arnold\n       </a>\n       , Richmond was burned by British troops, causing Governor\n       <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Jefferson" title="Thomas Jefferson">\n        Thomas Jefferson\n       </a>\n       to flee as the Virginia militia, led by\n       <a href="/wiki/Sampson_Mathews" title="Sampson Mathews">\n        Sampson Mathews\n       </a>\n       , defended the city.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Waddell_11-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Waddell-11">\n         [11]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Early_United_States">\n        Early United States\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Richmond,_Virginia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Early United States">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       Richmond recovered quickly from the war, and by 1782 was once again a thriving city.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Yorktown_1781_12-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Yorktown_1781-12">\n         [12]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In 1786, the\n       <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Statute_for_Religious_Freedom" title="Virginia Statute for Religious Freedom">\n        Virginia Statute for Religious Freedom\n       </a>\n       (drafted by\n       <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Jefferson" title="Thomas Jefferson">\n        Thomas Jefferson\n       </a>\n       , 1743-1826) was passed at the temporary capitol in Richmond, providing the basis for the separation of church and state, a key element in the development of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Freedom_of_religion" title="Freedom of religion">\n        freedom of religion\n       </a>\n       in the United States.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Religious_Freedom_13-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Religious_Freedom-13">\n         [13]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       A permanent home for the new government, the\n       <a href="/wiki/Greek_Revival_architecture" title="Greek Revival architecture">\n        Greek Revival style\n       </a>\n       of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Virginia_State_Capitol" title="Virginia State Capitol">\n        Virginia State Capitol\n       </a>\n       building, was designed by Thomas Jefferson with the assistance of\n       <a href="/wiki/Charles-Louis_Cl%C3%A9risseau" title="Charles-Louis Cl\xc3\xa9risseau">\n        Charles-Louis Cl\xc3\xa9risseau\n       </a>\n       , and was completed in 1788.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       After the\n       <a href="/wiki/American_Revolutionary_War" title="American Revolutionary War">\n        American Revolutionary War\n       </a>\n       (1775-1783), Richmond emerged as an important industrial center. To facilitate the transfer of cargo from the flat-bottomed\n       <a href="/wiki/James_River_bateau" title="James River bateau">\n        James River bateaux\n       </a>\n       above the fall line to the ocean-faring ships below, an enterprising\n       <a href="/wiki/George_Washington" title="George Washington">\n        George Washington\n       </a>\n       helped design the\n       <a href="/wiki/James_River_and_Kanawha_Canal" title="James River and Kanawha Canal">\n        James River and Kanawha Canal\n       </a>\n       from\n       <a href="/wiki/Westham,_Virginia" title="Westham, Virginia">\n        Westham\n       </a>\n       east to Richmond, in the 18th century to bypass Richmond\'s rapids on the upper James River with the intent of providing a water route across the\n       <a href="/wiki/Appalachian_Mountains" title="Appalachian Mountains">\n        Appalachian Mountains\n       </a>\n       to the\n       <a href="/wiki/Kanawha_River" title="Kanawha River">\n        Kanawha River\n       </a>\n       flowing westward into the\n       <a href="/wiki/Ohio_River" title="Ohio River">\n        Ohio\n       </a>\n       then eventually to the\n       <a href="/wiki/Mississippi_River" title="Mississippi River">\n        Mississippi River\n       </a>\n       . The legacy of the canal boatmen is represented by the figure in the center of the city flag. As a result of this and ample access to\n       <a href="/wiki/Hydropower" title="Hydropower">\n        hydropower\n       </a>\n       due to the falls, Richmond became home to some of the largest manufacturing facilities in the country, including iron works and flour mills, the largest facilities of their kind in\n       <a href="/wiki/Southeastern_United_States" title="Southeastern United States">\n        The South\n       </a>\n       . The resistance to the slave trade was growing by the mid-nineteenth century; in one famous case in 1848,\n       <a href="/wiki/Henry_Box_Brown" title="Henry Box Brown">\n        Henry "Box" Brown\n       </a>\n       made history by having himself nailed into a small box and shipped from Richmond through\n       <a href="/wiki/Baltimore" title="Baltimore">\n        Baltimore\n       </a>\n       \'s\n       <a href="/wiki/President_Street_Station" title="President Street Station">\n        President Street Station\n       </a>\n       northward on the\n       <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia,_Wilmington_and_Baltimore_Railroad" title="Philadelphia, Wilmington and Baltimore Railroad">\n        Philadelphia, Wilmington and Baltimore Railroad\n       </a>\n       (a well-used "\n       <a href="/wiki/Underground_Railroad" title="Underground Railroad">\n        Underground Railroad\n       </a>\n       " route for escaping disguised slaves) to abolitionists in\n       <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia" title="Philadelphia">\n        Philadelphia\n       </a>\n       , in the free state of\n       <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania" title="Pennsylvania">\n        Pennsylvania\n       </a>\n       , escaping slavery.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Brown_14-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Brown-14">\n         [14]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       By 1850, Richmond was connected by the\n       <a href="/wiki/Richmond_and_Petersburg_Railroad" title="Richmond and Petersburg Railroad">\n        Richmond and Petersburg Railroad\n       </a>\n       to\n       <a href="/wiki/Port_Walthall" title="Port Walthall">\n        Port Walthall\n       </a>\n       , where ships carrying over 200 tonnes of cargo could connect to\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Baltimore,_Maryland" title="Baltimore, Maryland">\n        Baltimore\n       </a>\n       or\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Philadelphia,_Pennsylvania" title="Philadelphia, Pennsylvania">\n        Philadelphia\n       </a>\n       or passenger liners could reach\n       <a href="/wiki/Norfolk,_Virginia" title="Norfolk, Virginia">\n        Norfolk, Virginia\n       </a>\n       through the\n       <a href="/wiki/Hampton_Roads" title="Hampton Roads">\n        Hampton Roads\n       </a>\n       harbor.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15">\n        <a href="#cite_note-15">\n         [15]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Civil_War">\n        Civil War\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Richmond,_Virginia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Civil War">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Richmond_in_the_American_Civil_War" title="Richmond in the American Civil War">\n        Richmond in the American Civil War\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Richmond_Virginia_damage2.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3652" data-file-width="5772" height="139" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Richmond_Virginia_damage2.jpg/220px-Richmond_Virginia_damage2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Richmond_Virginia_damage2.jpg/330px-Richmond_Virginia_damage2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Richmond_Virginia_damage2.jpg/440px-Richmond_Virginia_damage2.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Richmond_Virginia_damage2.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Retreating Confederates burned one-fourth of Richmond in April 1865\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       On April 17, 1861, five days after the Confederate attack on\n       <a href="/wiki/Fort_Sumter" title="Fort Sumter">\n        Fort Sumter\n       </a>\n       , the state legislature voted to secede from the\n       <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">\n        United States\n       </a>\n       and join the newly organized\n       <a href="/wiki/Confederate_States_of_America" title="Confederate States of America">\n        Confederate States of America\n       </a>\n       . Official action came in May, after the Confederacy promised to move its national capital from its provisional home in\n       <a href="/wiki/Montgomery,_Alabama" title="Montgomery, Alabama">\n        Montgomery, Alabama\n       </a>\n       to Richmond. The city was located at the end of a long supply line, which made it difficult to defend, requiring the bulk of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Army_of_Northern_Virginia" title="Army of Northern Virginia">\n        Army of Northern Virginia\n       </a>\n       and arguably the Confederacy\'s best troops and commanders.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16">\n        <a href="#cite_note-16">\n         [16]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       It became the main target of Union armies, especially in the campaigns of 1862 and 1864\xe2\x80\x9365.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In addition to Virginia and Confederate government offices and hospitals, a railroad hub, and one of the largest slave markets, Richmond had the largest iron foundry and arms factory during the war, the\n       <a href="/wiki/Tredegar_Iron_Works" title="Tredegar Iron Works">\n        Tredegar Iron Works\n       </a>\n       , which turned out artillery and other munitions, including the 723 tons of armor plating that covered the\n       <a href="/wiki/CSS_Virginia" title="CSS Virginia">\n        CSS Virginia\n       </a>\n       (former raised\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/USS_Merrimac" title="USS Merrimac">\n        USS Merrimac\n       </a>\n       steam frigate), the world\'s first\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ironclad" title="Ironclad">\n        ironclad\n       </a>\n       warship used in war, as well as much of the Confederates\' heavy\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ordnance_ammunition" title="Ordnance ammunition">\n        ordnance\n       </a>\n       machinery.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tredegar_17-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Tredegar-17">\n         [17]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Confederate_Congress" title="Confederate Congress">\n        Confederate States Congress\n       </a>\n       shared quarters with the\n       <a href="/wiki/Virginia_General_Assembly" title="Virginia General Assembly">\n        Virginia General Assembly\n       </a>\n       in\n       <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Jefferson" title="Thomas Jefferson">\n        Jefferson\'s\n       </a>\n       designed\n       <a href="/wiki/Virginia_State_Capitol" title="Virginia State Capitol">\n        Virginia State Capitol\n       </a>\n       , with the Confederacy\'s executive mansion, known as the "\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Museum_of_the_Confederacy" title="Museum of the Confederacy">\n        White House of the Confederacy\n       </a>\n       ", located two blocks away on Clay Street. The\n       <a href="/wiki/Seven_Days_Battles" title="Seven Days Battles">\n        Seven Days Battles\n       </a>\n       followed in late June and early July 1862, during which commanding Union General-in-Chief\n       <a href="/wiki/George_B._McClellan" title="George B. McClellan">\n        George B. McClellan\n       </a>\n       threatened to take Richmond in the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Peninsula_campaign" title="Peninsula campaign">\n        Peninsula campaign\n       </a>\n       but ultimately failed.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Three years later, as March 1865 ended, Richmond became indefensible after nearby\n       <a href="/wiki/Petersburg,_Virginia" title="Petersburg, Virginia">\n        Petersburg\n       </a>\n       and several remaining rail supply lines to the south and southwest were broken. On March 25, Confederate General\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/John_B._Gordon" title="John B. Gordon">\n        John B. Gordon\n       </a>\n       \'s desperate attack on\n       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Fort_Stedman" title="Battle of Fort Stedman">\n        Fort Stedman\n       </a>\n       east of Petersburg failed. On April 1, Federal Cavalry General\n       <a href="/wiki/Philip_Sheridan" title="Philip Sheridan">\n        Philip Sheridan\n       </a>\n       , assigned to interdict the Southside Railroad, met brigades commanded by Southern Gen.\n       <a href="/wiki/George_Pickett" title="George Pickett">\n        George Pickett\n       </a>\n       at the\n       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Five_Forks" title="Battle of Five Forks">\n        Five Forks\n       </a>\n       junction, smashing them, taking thousands of prisoners, and encouraging Union General-in-Chief\n       <a href="/wiki/Ulysses_S._Grant" title="Ulysses S. Grant">\n        Ulysses S. Grant\n       </a>\n       to order a general advance. When the Union Sixth Corps broke through Confederate lines on the Boydton Plank Road south of Petersburg, Confederate casualties exceeded 5,000, or about a tenth of General Lee\'s defending army. Lee then informed President\n       <a href="/wiki/Jefferson_Davis" title="Jefferson Davis">\n        Jefferson Davis\n       </a>\n       that he was about to evacuate Richmond.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18">\n        <a href="#cite_note-18">\n         [18]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Davis and his cabinet, along with the government archives and Treasury gold, left the city by train that night, as government officials burned documents and departing Confederate troops burned tobacco and other warehouses to deny their contents to the victors. On April 2, 1865, General\n       <a href="/wiki/Godfrey_Weitzel" title="Godfrey Weitzel">\n        Godfrey Weitzel\n       </a>\n       , commander of the 25th Corps of the\n       <a href="/wiki/United_States_Colored_Troops" title="United States Colored Troops">\n        United States Colored Troops\n       </a>\n       , accepted the city\'s surrender from the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mayor_of_Richmond" title="Mayor of Richmond">\n        Mayor\n       </a>\n       and a group of leading citizens who remained.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19">\n        <a href="#cite_note-19">\n         [19]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The Union troops eventually managed to stop the raging fires but about 25% of the city\'s buildings were destroyed.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20">\n        <a href="#cite_note-20">\n         [20]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       President\n       <a href="/wiki/Abraham_Lincoln" title="Abraham Lincoln">\n        Abraham Lincoln\n       </a>\n       visited General Grant at Petersburg on April 3, and took a launch to Richmond up the\n       <a href="/wiki/James_River" title="James River">\n        James River\n       </a>\n       the next day, while Jefferson Davis attempted to organize his remaining Confederate government further southwest at\n       <a href="/wiki/Danville,_Virginia" title="Danville, Virginia">\n        Danville\n       </a>\n       . Lincoln met Confederate assistant secretary of War\n       <a href="/wiki/John_Archibald_Campbell" title="John Archibald Campbell">\n        John A. Campbell\n       </a>\n       , and handed him a note inviting Virginia\'s state legislature to end their rebellion. After Campbell spun the note to Confederate legislators as a possible end to the\n       <a href="/wiki/Emancipation_Proclamation" title="Emancipation Proclamation">\n        Emancipation Proclamation\n       </a>\n       , Lincoln rescinded his offer and ordered General Weitzel to prevent the former Confederate state legislature from meeting. Union forces killed, wounded or captured 8,000 Confederate troops at\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Battle_of_Sayler%27s_Creek" title="Battle of Sayler\'s Creek">\n        Sayler\'s Creek\n       </a>\n       southwest of Petersburg on April 6, as the Southerners continued a general retreat southwestward. General Lee continued to reject General Grant\'s surrender suggestions until Sheridan\'s infantry and cavalry moved around the shrinking\n       <a href="/wiki/Army_of_Northern_Virginia" title="Army of Northern Virginia">\n        Army of Northern Virginia\n       </a>\n       and appeared in front of his withdrawing forces on April 8, cutting off the line of further retreat southwest. He surrendered his remaining approximately 10,000 troops at\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Appomattox_Court_House,_Virginia" title="Appomattox Court House, Virginia">\n        Appomattox Court House\n       </a>\n       meeting General Grant the following morning at the McLean Home.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21">\n        <a href="#cite_note-21">\n         [21]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Davis was captured on May 10th near\n       <a href="/wiki/Irwinville,_Georgia" title="Irwinville, Georgia">\n        Irwinville, Georgia\n       </a>\n       and taken back to Virginia, where he was imprisoned for two years at\n       <a href="/wiki/Fort_Monroe" title="Fort Monroe">\n        Fort Monroe\n       </a>\n       until freed on bail.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22">\n        <a href="#cite_note-22">\n         [22]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Postbellum">\n        Postbellum\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Richmond,_Virginia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Postbellum">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       Richmond emerged a decade after the smoldering rubble of the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_States_Civil_War" title="United States Civil War">\n        Civil War\n       </a>\n       to resume its position as an economic powerhouse, with iron front buildings and massive brick factories. Canal traffic peaked in the 1860s and slowly gave way to railroads, allowing Richmond to become a major railroad crossroads, eventually including the site of the world\'s first triple railroad crossing.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-JR.26kanawha_23-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-JR.26kanawha-23">\n         [23]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Tobacco warehousing and processing continued to play a role, boosted by the world\'s first cigarette-rolling machine, invented by\n       <a href="/wiki/James_Albert_Bonsack" title="James Albert Bonsack">\n        James Albert Bonsack\n       </a>\n       of\n       <a href="/wiki/Roanoke,_Virginia" title="Roanoke, Virginia">\n        Roanoke\n       </a>\n       in 1880/81. Contributing to Richmond\'s resurgence was the first successful electrically powered\n       <a href="/wiki/Tram" title="Tram">\n        trolley\n       </a>\n       system in the United States, the\n       <a href="/wiki/Richmond_Union_Passenger_Railway" title="Richmond Union Passenger Railway">\n        Richmond Union Passenger Railway\n       </a>\n       . Designed by electric power pioneer\n       <a href="/wiki/Frank_J._Sprague" title="Frank J. Sprague">\n        Frank J. Sprague\n       </a>\n       , the trolley system opened its first line in 1888, and electric streetcar lines rapidly spread to other cities across the country.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-streetcar_1_24-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-streetcar_1-24">\n         [24]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Sprague\'s system used an overhead wire and trolley pole to collect current, with electric motors on the car\'s trucks.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-streetcar_2_25-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-streetcar_2-25">\n         [25]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In Richmond, the transition from streetcars to buses began in May 1947 and was completed on November 25, 1949.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26">\n        <a href="#cite_note-26">\n         [26]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="20th_century">\n        20th century\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Richmond,_Virginia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: 20th century">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:14th_Street_Bridge,_Richmond,_ca_1917.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="448" data-file-width="735" height="134" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/14th_Street_Bridge%2C_Richmond%2C_ca_1917.jpg/220px-14th_Street_Bridge%2C_Richmond%2C_ca_1917.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/14th_Street_Bridge%2C_Richmond%2C_ca_1917.jpg/330px-14th_Street_Bridge%2C_Richmond%2C_ca_1917.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/14th_Street_Bridge%2C_Richmond%2C_ca_1917.jpg/440px-14th_Street_Bridge%2C_Richmond%2C_ca_1917.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:14th_Street_Bridge,_Richmond,_ca_1917.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         By the early 20th century, Richmond had an extensive network of electric streetcars, as shown here crossing the Mayo Bridge across the James River, ca. 1917\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       By the beginning of the 20th century, the city\'s population had reached 85,050 in 5 square miles (13\xc2\xa0km\n       <sup>\n        2\n       </sup>\n       ), making it the most densely populated city in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Southern_United_States" title="Southern United States">\n        Southern United States\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GibsonC_27-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-GibsonC-27">\n         [27]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In 1900, the Census Bureau reported Richmond\'s population as 62.1% white and 37.9% black.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-census1_28-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-census1-28">\n         [28]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Freed slaves and their descendants created a thriving African-American business community, and the city\'s historic\n       <a href="/wiki/Jackson_Ward" title="Jackson Ward">\n        Jackson Ward\n       </a>\n       became known as the "Wall Street of Black America." In 1903, African-American businesswoman and financier\n       <a href="/wiki/Maggie_L._Walker" title="Maggie L. Walker">\n        Maggie L. Walker\n       </a>\n       chartered St. Luke Penny Savings Bank, and served as its first president, as well as the first female bank president in the United States. Today, the bank is called the Consolidated Bank and Trust Company, and it is the oldest surviving African-American bank in the U.S.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MaggieWalker_29-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-MaggieWalker-29">\n         [29]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Other figures from this time included\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/John_Mitchell,_Jr." title="John Mitchell, Jr.">\n        John Mitchell, Jr.\n       </a>\n       In 1910, the former city of\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Manchester,_Virginia" title="Manchester, Virginia">\n        Manchester\n       </a>\n       was consolidated with the city of Richmond, and in 1914, the city annexed Barton Heights, Ginter Park, and Highland Park areas of\n       <a href="/wiki/Henrico_County,_Virginia" title="Henrico County, Virginia">\n        Henrico County\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-manchester_30-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-manchester-30">\n         [30]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In May 1914, Richmond became the headquarters of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Federal_Reserve_Bank_of_Richmond" title="Federal Reserve Bank of Richmond">\n        Fifth District of the Federal Reserve Bank\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Several major performing arts venues were constructed during the 1920s, including what are now the Landmark Theatre, Byrd Theatre, and Carpenter Theatre. The city\'s first radio station,\n       <a href="/wiki/WRVA_(AM)" title="WRVA (AM)">\n        WRVA\n       </a>\n       , began broadcasting in 1925.\n       <a href="/wiki/WTVR-TV" title="WTVR-TV">\n        WTVR-TV\n       </a>\n       (CBS 6), the first television station in Richmond, was the first television station south of Washington, D.C.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WRVA_31-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-WRVA-31">\n         [31]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Between 1963 and 1965, there was a "downtown boom" that led to the construction of more than 700 buildings in the city. In 1968,\n       <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Commonwealth_University" title="Virginia Commonwealth University">\n        Virginia Commonwealth University\n       </a>\n       was created by the merger of the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Medical_College_of_Virginia" title="Medical College of Virginia">\n        Medical College of Virginia\n       </a>\n       with the\n       <a href="/wiki/Richmond_Professional_Institute" title="Richmond Professional Institute">\n        Richmond Professional Institute\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-vcu_32-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-vcu-32">\n         [32]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In 1970, Richmond\'s borders expanded by an additional 27 square miles (70\xc2\xa0km\n       <sup>\n        2\n       </sup>\n       ) on the south. After several years of court cases in which\n       <a href="/wiki/Chesterfield_County,_Virginia" title="Chesterfield County, Virginia">\n        Chesterfield County\n       </a>\n       fought annexation, more than 47,000 people who once were Chesterfield County residents found themselves within the city\'s perimeters on January 1, 1970.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RichmondvUS_33-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-RichmondvUS-33">\n         [33]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In 1996, still-sore tensions arose amid controversy involved in placing a statue of African American Richmond native and tennis star\n       <a href="/wiki/Arthur_Ashe" title="Arthur Ashe">\n        Arthur Ashe\n       </a>\n       to the series of statues of Confederate Generals of the Civil War on\n       <a href="/wiki/Monument_Avenue" title="Monument Avenue">\n        Monument Avenue\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-arthurashe_34-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-arthurashe-34">\n         [34]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       After several months of controversy, the bronze statue of Ashe was finally completed on Monument Avenue facing the opposite direction from the Confederate Generals on July 10, 1996.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-arthurashe2_35-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-arthurashe2-35">\n         [35]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       A multimillion-dollar flood wall was completed in 1995, in order to protect low-lying areas of city from the oft-rising waters of the James River. As a result, the River District businesses grew rapidly, and today the area is home to much of Richmond\'s entertainment, dining and nightlife activity, bolstered by the creation of a Canal Walk along the city\'s former industrial canals.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-floodwall_36-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-floodwall-36">\n         [36]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-canal_walk_37-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-canal_walk-37">\n         [37]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Geography_and_climate">\n        Geography and climate\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Richmond,_Virginia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Geography and climate">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:RichmondVAFromTheISS.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="679" data-file-width="1024" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/RichmondVAFromTheISS.jpg/220px-RichmondVAFromTheISS.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/RichmondVAFromTheISS.jpg/330px-RichmondVAFromTheISS.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/RichmondVAFromTheISS.jpg/440px-RichmondVAFromTheISS.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:RichmondVAFromTheISS.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         The Richmond area, seen from the\n         <a href="/wiki/International_Space_Station" title="International Space Station">\n          International Space Station\n         </a>\n         in early-April 2013.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       See also:\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Richmond-Petersburg" title="Richmond-Petersburg">\n        Richmond-Petersburg\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Richmond is located at\n       <span class="plainlinks nourlexpansion">\n        <a class="external text" href="//tools.wmflabs.org/geohack/geohack.php?pagename=Richmond,_Virginia&amp;params=37_32_N_77_28_W_region:US">\n         <span class="geo-default">\n          <span class="geo-dms" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location">\n           <span class="latitude">\n            37\xc2\xb032\xe2\x80\xb2N\n           </span>\n           <span class="longitude">\n            77\xc2\xb028\xe2\x80\xb2W\n           </span>\n          </span>\n         </span>\n         <span class="geo-multi-punct">\n          \xef\xbb\xbf / \xef\xbb\xbf\n         </span>\n         <span class="geo-nondefault">\n          <span class="geo-dec" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location">\n           37.533\xc2\xb0N 77.467\xc2\xb0W\n          </span>\n          <span style="display:none">\n           \xef\xbb\xbf /\n           <span class="geo">\n            37.533; -77.467\n           </span>\n          </span>\n         </span>\n        </a>\n       </span>\n       (37.538, \xe2\x88\x9277.462). According to the\n       <a href="/wiki/United_States_Census_Bureau" title="United States Census Bureau">\n        United States Census Bureau\n       </a>\n       , the city has a total area of 62 square miles (160\xc2\xa0km\n       <sup>\n        2\n       </sup>\n       ), of which 60 square miles (160\xc2\xa0km\n       <sup>\n        2\n       </sup>\n       ) is land and 2.7 square miles (7.0\xc2\xa0km\n       <sup>\n        2\n       </sup>\n       ) of it (4.3%) is water.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GR1_38-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-GR1-38">\n         [38]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The city is located in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Piedmont_region_of_Virginia" title="Piedmont region of Virginia">\n        Piedmont region of Virginia\n       </a>\n       , at the highest navigable point of the James River. The Piedmont region is characterized by relatively low, rolling hills, and lies between the low, flat\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tidewater_region_of_Virginia" title="Tidewater region of Virginia">\n        Tidewater\n       </a>\n       region and the\n       <a href="/wiki/Blue_Ridge_Mountains" title="Blue Ridge Mountains">\n        Blue Ridge Mountains\n       </a>\n       . Significant bodies of water in the region include the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/James_River_(Virginia)" title="James River (Virginia)">\n        James River\n       </a>\n       , the\n       <a href="/wiki/Appomattox_River" title="Appomattox River">\n        Appomattox River\n       </a>\n       , and the\n       <a href="/wiki/Chickahominy_River" title="Chickahominy River">\n        Chickahominy River\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Richmond-Petersburg" title="Richmond-Petersburg">\n        Richmond-Petersburg\n       </a>\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_States_metropolitan_area" title="United States metropolitan area">\n        Metropolitan Statistical Area\n       </a>\n       (MSA), the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_United_States_metropolitan_statistical_areas_by_population" title="List of United States metropolitan statistical areas by population">\n        44th largest\n       </a>\n       in the United States, includes the independent cities of Richmond,\n       <a href="/wiki/Colonial_Heights,_Virginia" title="Colonial Heights, Virginia">\n        Colonial Heights\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Hopewell,_Virginia" title="Hopewell, Virginia">\n        Hopewell\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Petersburg,_Virginia" title="Petersburg, Virginia">\n        Petersburg\n       </a>\n       , as well as the counties of\n       <a href="/wiki/Charles_City_County,_Virginia" title="Charles City County, Virginia">\n        Charles City\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Chesterfield_County,_Virginia" title="Chesterfield County, Virginia">\n        Chesterfield\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Dinwiddie_County,_Virginia" title="Dinwiddie County, Virginia">\n        Dinwiddie\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Goochland_County,_Virginia" title="Goochland County, Virginia">\n        Goochland\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Hanover_County,_Virginia" title="Hanover County, Virginia">\n        Hanover\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Henrico_County,_Virginia" title="Henrico County, Virginia">\n        Henrico\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/New_Kent_County,_Virginia" title="New Kent County, Virginia">\n        New Kent\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Powhatan_County,_Virginia" title="Powhatan County, Virginia">\n        Powhatan\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Prince_George_County,_Virginia" title="Prince George County, Virginia">\n        Prince George\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RIPE_report_39-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-RIPE_report-39">\n         [39]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       As of July 1, 2009\n       <sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;">\n        <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Richmond,_Virginia&amp;action=edit">\n         [update]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       , the total population of the Richmond\xe2\x80\x94Petersburg\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Metropolitan_Statistical_Area" title="Metropolitan Statistical Area">\n        MSA\n       </a>\n       was 1,258,251.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Cityscape">\n        Cityscape\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Richmond,_Virginia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Cityscape">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:RichmondNSEW.png">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="566" data-file-width="684" height="182" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/RichmondNSEW.png/220px-RichmondNSEW.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/RichmondNSEW.png/330px-RichmondNSEW.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/RichmondNSEW.png/440px-RichmondNSEW.png 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:RichmondNSEW.png" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Richmond is often subdivided into\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/North_Side_(Richmond_Virginia)" title="North Side (Richmond Virginia)">\n          North Side\n         </a>\n         ,\n         <a href="/wiki/Southside_(Richmond,_Virginia)" title="Southside (Richmond, Virginia)">\n          Southside\n         </a>\n         ,\n         <a href="/wiki/East_End_(Richmond,_Virginia)" title="East End (Richmond, Virginia)">\n          East End\n         </a>\n         , and\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_West_End_(Richmond,_Virginia)" title="The West End (Richmond, Virginia)">\n          West End\n         </a>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       See also:\n       <a href="/wiki/Neighborhoods_of_Richmond,_Virginia" title="Neighborhoods of Richmond, Virginia">\n        Neighborhoods of Richmond, Virginia\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Richmond\'s original street grid, laid out in 1737, included the area between what are now Broad, 17th, and 25th Streets and the James River. Modern\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Downtown_Richmond" title="Downtown Richmond">\n        Downtown Richmond\n       </a>\n       is located slightly farther west, on the slopes of Shockoe Hill. Nearby neighborhoods include\n       <a href="/wiki/Shockoe_Bottom" title="Shockoe Bottom">\n        Shockoe Bottom\n       </a>\n       , the historically significant and low-lying area between Shockoe Hill and\n       <a href="/wiki/Church_Hill" title="Church Hill">\n        Church Hill\n       </a>\n       , and Monroe Ward, which contains the\n       <a href="/wiki/Jefferson_Hotel_(Richmond,_Virginia)" title="Jefferson Hotel (Richmond, Virginia)">\n        Jefferson Hotel\n       </a>\n       . Richmond\'s East End includes neighborhoods like rapidly gentrifying\n       <a href="/wiki/Church_Hill" title="Church Hill">\n        Church Hill\n       </a>\n       , home to\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/St._John%27s_Episcopal_Church,_Richmond,_Virginia" title="St. John\'s Episcopal Church, Richmond, Virginia">\n        St. John\'s Church\n       </a>\n       , as well as poorer areas like\n       <a href="/wiki/Fulton_Hill" title="Fulton Hill">\n        Fulton\n       </a>\n       , Union Hill, and Fairmont, and public housing projects like\n       <a href="/wiki/Mosby_Court" title="Mosby Court">\n        Mosby Court\n       </a>\n       , Whitcomb Court, Fairfield Court, and Creighton Court closer to\n       <a href="/wiki/Interstate_64" title="Interstate 64">\n        Interstate 64\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-neighborhoods_40-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-neighborhoods-40">\n         [40]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The area between Belvidere Street,\n       <a href="/wiki/Interstate_195_(Virginia)" title="Interstate 195 (Virginia)">\n        Interstate 195\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Interstate_95_in_Virginia" title="Interstate 95 in Virginia">\n        Interstate 95\n       </a>\n       , and the river, which includes\n       <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Commonwealth_University" title="Virginia Commonwealth University">\n        Virginia Commonwealth University\n       </a>\n       , is socioeconomically and architecturally diverse. North of Broad Street, the Carver and Newtowne West neighborhoods are demographically similar to neighboring\n       <a href="/wiki/Jackson_Ward" title="Jackson Ward">\n        Jackson Ward\n       </a>\n       , with Carver experiencing some gentrification due to its proximity to VCU. The affluent area between the\n       <a href="/wiki/Boulevard_(Richmond,_Virginia)" title="Boulevard (Richmond, Virginia)">\n        Boulevard\n       </a>\n       , Main Street, Broad Street, and VCU, known as the\n       <a href="/wiki/Fan_district" title="Fan district">\n        Fan\n       </a>\n       , is home to\n       <a href="/wiki/Monument_Avenue" title="Monument Avenue">\n        Monument Avenue\n       </a>\n       , an outstanding collection of\n       <a href="/wiki/Victorian_architecture" title="Victorian architecture">\n        Victorian architecture\n       </a>\n       , and many students. West of the Boulevard is the Museum District, the location of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Historical_Society" title="Virginia Historical Society">\n        Virginia Historical Society\n       </a>\n       and the\n       <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Museum_of_Fine_Arts" title="Virginia Museum of Fine Arts">\n        Virginia Museum of Fine Arts\n       </a>\n       . South of the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Downtown_Expressway" title="Downtown Expressway">\n        Downtown Expressway\n       </a>\n       are\n       <a href="/wiki/Byrd_Park" title="Byrd Park">\n        Byrd Park\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Maymont" title="Maymont">\n        Maymont\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Hollywood_Cemetery_(Richmond,_Virginia)" title="Hollywood Cemetery (Richmond, Virginia)">\n        Hollywood Cemetery\n       </a>\n       , the predominantly black working class Randolph neighborhood, and white working class\n       <a href="/wiki/Oregon_Hill" title="Oregon Hill">\n        Oregon Hill\n       </a>\n       . Cary Street between Interstate 195 and the\n       <a href="/wiki/Boulevard_(Richmond,_Virginia)" title="Boulevard (Richmond, Virginia)">\n        Boulevard\n       </a>\n       is a popular commercial area called\n       <a href="/wiki/Carytown,_Richmond,_Virginia" title="Carytown, Richmond, Virginia">\n        Carytown\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-neighborhoods_40-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-neighborhoods-40">\n         [40]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tleft">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Richmond,_Virginia_(8127317299).jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2304" data-file-width="3072" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Richmond%2C_Virginia_%288127317299%29.jpg/220px-Richmond%2C_Virginia_%288127317299%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Richmond%2C_Virginia_%288127317299%29.jpg/330px-Richmond%2C_Virginia_%288127317299%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Richmond%2C_Virginia_%288127317299%29.jpg/440px-Richmond%2C_Virginia_%288127317299%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Richmond,_Virginia_(8127317299).jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         View of the Carillon from across the James River\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Richmond\'s Northside is home to numerous listed historic districts.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41">\n        <a href="#cite_note-41">\n         [41]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Neighborhoods such as\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chestnut_Hill-Plateau_Historic_District_(Richmond,_VA)" title="Chestnut Hill-Plateau Historic District (Richmond, VA)">\n        Chestnut Hill-Plateau\n       </a>\n       and Barton Heights began to develop at the end of the 19th century when the new streetcar system made it possible for people to live on the outskirts of town and still commute to jobs downtown. Other prominent Northside neighborhoods include Azalea, Barton Heights, Bellevue, Chamberlayne, Ginter Park, Highland Park, and Rosedale.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-neighborhoods_40-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-neighborhoods-40">\n         [40]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Farther west is the affluent, suburban\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_West_End_(Richmond,_Virginia)" title="The West End (Richmond, Virginia)">\n        West End\n       </a>\n       . Windsor Farms is among its best-known sections. The West End also includes middle to lower income neighborhoods, such as Laurel, Farmington and the areas surrounding the Regency Mall. More affluent areas include Glen Allen, Short Pump, and the areas of Tuckahoe away from Regency Mall, which can all be found north and northwest of the city. The\n       <a href="/wiki/University_of_Richmond" title="University of Richmond">\n        University of Richmond\n       </a>\n       and the Country Club of Virginia can be found here as well, which are located just inside the City Limits.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-neighborhoods_40-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-neighborhoods-40">\n         [40]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The portion of the city south of the James River is known as the Southside. Neighborhoods in the city\'s Southside area range from affluent and middle class suburban neighborhoods Westover Hills, Forest Hill, Southampton, Stratford Hills, Oxford, Huguenot Hills, Hobby Hill, and Woodland Heights to the impoverished\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Manchester,_Virginia" title="Manchester, Virginia">\n        Manchester\n       </a>\n       and Blackwell areas, the Hillside Court housing projects, and the ailing Jefferson Davis Highway commercial corridor. Other Southside neighborhoods include Fawnbrook, Broad Rock, Cherry Gardens, Cullenwood, and Beaufont Hills. Much of Southside developed a suburban character as part of\n       <a href="/wiki/Chesterfield_County,_Virginia" title="Chesterfield County, Virginia">\n        Chesterfield County\n       </a>\n       before being annexed by Richmond, most notably in 1970.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-neighborhoods_40-4">\n        <a href="#cite_note-neighborhoods-40">\n         [40]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">\n        Climate\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Richmond,_Virginia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Climate">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Richmond_After_the_Flood_(7790622530).jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4350" data-file-width="5550" height="172" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Richmond_After_the_Flood_%287790622530%29.jpg/220px-Richmond_After_the_Flood_%287790622530%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Richmond_After_the_Flood_%287790622530%29.jpg/330px-Richmond_After_the_Flood_%287790622530%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Richmond_After_the_Flood_%287790622530%29.jpg/440px-Richmond_After_the_Flood_%287790622530%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Richmond_After_the_Flood_(7790622530).jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Flooding of Old Manchester during\n         <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Agnes" title="Hurricane Agnes">\n          Hurricane Agnes\n         </a>\n         , 1972\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Richmond has a Warm Temperate Climate and a\n       <a href="/wiki/Humid_subtropical_climate" title="Humid subtropical climate">\n        humid subtropical climate\n       </a>\n       (\n       <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="K\xc3\xb6ppen climate classification">\n        K\xc3\xb6ppen\n       </a>\n       <i>\n        Cfa\n       </i>\n       ), with hot and humid summers and generally cold winters. The mountains to the west act as a partial barrier to outbreaks of cold, continental air in winter; Arctic air is delayed long enough to be modified, then further warmed as it subsides in its approach to Richmond. The open waters of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Chesapeake_Bay" title="Chesapeake Bay">\n        Chesapeake Bay\n       </a>\n       and Atlantic Ocean contribute to the humid summers and mild winters. The coldest weather normally occurs from late December to early February, and the January daily mean temperature is 37.9\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0F (3.3\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C), with an average of 6.0 days with highs at or below the freezing mark.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NWS_Wakefield.2C_VA_.28AKQ.291_42-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-NWS_Wakefield.2C_VA_.28AKQ.291-42">\n         [42]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Downtown areas and suburbs to the east of Richmond are situated in USDA\n       <a href="/wiki/Hardiness_zone" title="Hardiness zone">\n        Hardiness zones\n       </a>\n       7b while surrounding suburban and rural areas to the west are in the 7a Hardiness Zone.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USDA_PlantHardiness_43-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-USDA_PlantHardiness-43">\n         [43]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and temperatures seldom lower to 0\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0F (\xe2\x88\x9218\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C), with the most recent subzero (\xc2\xb0F) reading occurring on January 28, 2000, when the temperature reached \xe2\x88\x921\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0F (\xe2\x88\x9218\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FAQs_.26_HOLIDAY_CLIMATOLOGY_RICHMOND_44-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-FAQs_.26_HOLIDAY_CLIMATOLOGY_RICHMOND-44">\n         [44]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The July daily mean temperature is 79.3\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0F (26.3\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C), and high temperatures reach or exceed 90\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0F (32\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C) approximately 43 days out of the year; while 100\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0F (38\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C) temperatures are not uncommon, they do not occur every year.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45">\n        <a href="#cite_note-45">\n         [45]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Extremes in temperature have ranged from \xe2\x88\x9212\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0F (\xe2\x88\x9224\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C) on January 19, 1940 up to 107\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0F (42\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C) on August 6, 1918.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47">\n        <a href="#cite_note-47">\n         [a]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Precipitation_(meteorology)" title="Precipitation (meteorology)">\n        Precipitation\n       </a>\n       is rather uniformly distributed throughout the year. However, dry periods lasting several weeks do occur, especially in autumn when long periods of pleasant, mild weather are most common. There is considerable variability in total monthly amounts from year to year so that no one month can be depended upon to be normal. Snow has been recorded during seven of the twelve months. Falls of 3 inches (7.6\xc2\xa0cm) or more within 24 hours occur an average once per year.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NWS_Wakefield.2C_VA_.28AKQ.291_42-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-NWS_Wakefield.2C_VA_.28AKQ.291-42">\n         [42]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Annual snowfall, however, is usually light, averaging 10.5 inches (27\xc2\xa0cm) per season.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NWS_Wakefield.2C_VA_.28AKQ.291_42-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-NWS_Wakefield.2C_VA_.28AKQ.291-42">\n         [42]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Snow typically remains on the ground only one or two days at a time, but remained for 16 days in 2010 (January 30 to February 14). Ice storms (freezing rain or glaze) are not uncommon, but they are seldom severe enough to do any considerable damage.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/James_River" title="James River">\n        James River\n       </a>\n       reaches tidewater at Richmond where flooding may occur in every month of the year, most frequently in March and least in July.\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hurricanes" title="Hurricanes">\n        Hurricanes\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tropical_storms" title="Tropical storms">\n        tropical storms\n       </a>\n       have been responsible for most of the flooding during the summer and early fall months. Hurricanes passing near Richmond have produced record rainfalls. In 1955, three hurricanes brought record rainfall to Richmond within a six-week period. The most noteworthy of these were\n       <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Connie" title="Hurricane Connie">\n        Hurricane Connie\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Diane" title="Hurricane Diane">\n        Hurricane Diane\n       </a>\n       that brought heavy rains five days apart. And in 2004, the downtown area suffered extensive flood damage after the remnants of\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hurricane_Gaston" title="Hurricane Gaston">\n        Hurricane Gaston\n       </a>\n       dumped up to 12 inches (300\xc2\xa0mm) of rainfall.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48">\n        <a href="#cite_note-48">\n         [47]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Damaging storms occur mainly from snow and\n       <a href="/wiki/Freezing_rain" title="Freezing rain">\n        freezing rain\n       </a>\n       in winter and from hurricanes, tornadoes, and severe thunderstorms in other seasons. Damage may be from wind, flooding, or rain, or from any combination of these.\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tornadoes" title="Tornadoes">\n        Tornadoes\n       </a>\n       are infrequent but some notable occurrences have been observed within the Richmond area.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Based on the 1981\xe2\x80\x932010 period, the average first occurrence of at or below freezing temperatures in the fall is November 4 and the average last occurrence in the spring is April 5.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FAQs_.26_HOLIDAY_CLIMATOLOGY_RICHMOND_44-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-FAQs_.26_HOLIDAY_CLIMATOLOGY_RICHMOND-44">\n         [44]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <table     <td style="padding-left:8px;">\n         204,214\n        </td>\n        <td style="font-size:85%">\n        </td>\n        <td style="padding-left:8px; text-align: center;">\n         3.2%\n
