href="/wiki/C-SPAN" title="C-SPAN">\n          C-SPAN\n         </a>\n         , January 25, 2017.\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Museums_and_monuments">\n        Museums and monuments\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Richmond,_Virginia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Museums and monuments">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Virginia_Museum_of_Fine_Arts_(historic_entrance).JPG">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2448" data-file-width="3264" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Virginia_Museum_of_Fine_Arts_%28historic_entrance%29.JPG/220px-Virginia_Museum_of_Fine_Arts_%28historic_entrance%29.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Virginia_Museum_of_Fine_Arts_%28historic_entrance%29.JPG/330px-Virginia_Museum_of_Fine_Arts_%28historic_entrance%29.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Virginia_Museum_of_Fine_Arts_%28historic_entrance%29.JPG/440px-Virginia_Museum_of_Fine_Arts_%28historic_entrance%29.JPG 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Virginia_Museum_of_Fine_Arts_(historic_entrance).JPG" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         1936 entrance to the\n         <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Museum_of_Fine_Arts" title="Virginia Museum of Fine Arts">\n          Virginia Museum of Fine Arts\n         </a>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Several of the city\'s large general museums are located near the Boulevard. On Boulevard proper are the\n       <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Historical_Society" title="Virginia Historical Society">\n        Virginia Historical Society\n       </a>\n       and the\n       <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Museum_of_Fine_Arts" title="Virginia Museum of Fine Arts">\n        Virginia Museum of Fine Arts\n       </a>\n       , lending their name to what is sometimes called the Museum District. Nearby on Broad Street is the\n       <a href="/wiki/Science_Museum_of_Virginia" title="Science Museum of Virginia">\n        Science Museum of Virginia\n       </a>\n       , housed in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Neoclassicism" title="Neoclassicism">\n        neoclassical\n       </a>\n       former 1919 Broad Street Union Station. Immediately adjacent is the\n       <a href="/wiki/Children%27s_Museum_of_Richmond" title="Children\'s Museum of Richmond">\n        Children\'s Museum of Richmond\n       </a>\n       , and two blocks away, the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Virginia_Center_for_Architecture" title="Virginia Center for Architecture">\n        Virginia Center for Architecture\n       </a>\n       . Within the downtown are the\n       <a href="/wiki/Library_of_Virginia" title="Library of Virginia">\n        Library of Virginia\n       </a>\n       and the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Valentine_Richmond_History_Center" title="Valentine Richmond History Center">\n        Valentine Richmond History Center\n       </a>\n       . Elsewhere are the\n       <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Holocaust_Museum" title="Virginia Holocaust Museum">\n        Virginia Holocaust Museum\n       </a>\n       and the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Old_Dominion_Railway_Museum" title="Old Dominion Railway Museum">\n        Old Dominion Railway Museum\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Richmond is home to museums and battlefields of the American Civil War. Near the riverfront is the\n       <a href="/wiki/Richmond_National_Battlefield_Park" title="Richmond National Battlefield Park">\n        Richmond National Battlefield Park\n       </a>\n       Visitors Center and the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/American_Civil_War_Center_at_Historic_Tredegar" title="American Civil War Center at Historic Tredegar">\n        American Civil War Center at Historic Tredegar\n       </a>\n       , both housed in the former buildings of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Tredegar_Iron_Works" title="Tredegar Iron Works">\n        Tredegar Iron Works\n       </a>\n       , where much of the ordnance for the war was produced. In\n       <a href="/wiki/Court_End" title="Court End">\n        Court End\n       </a>\n       , near the\n       <a href="/wiki/Virginia_State_Capitol" title="Virginia State Capitol">\n        Virginia State Capitol\n       </a>\n       , is the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Museum_of_the_Confederacy" title="Museum of the Confederacy">\n        Museum of the Confederacy\n       </a>\n       , along with the Davis Mansion, also known as the White House of the Confederacy; both feature a wide variety of objects and material from the era. The temporary home of former General Robert E. Lee still stands on Franklin Street in downtown Richmond. The history of slavery and emancipation are also increasingly represented: there is a former slave trail along the river that leads to Ancarrow\'s Boat Ramp and Historic Site which has been developed with interpretive signage, and in 2007, the Reconciliation Statue was placed in Shockoe Bottom, with parallel statues placed in\n       <a href="/wiki/Liverpool" title="Liverpool">\n        Liverpool\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Benin" title="Benin">\n        Benin\n       </a>\n       representing points of the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Triangle_Trade" title="Triangle Trade">\n        Triangle Trade\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Other historical points of interest include\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/St._John%27s_Episcopal_Church,_Richmond,_Virginia" title="St. John\'s Episcopal Church, Richmond, Virginia">\n        St. John\'s Church\n       </a>\n       , the site of\n       <a href="/wiki/Patrick_Henry" title="Patrick Henry">\n        Patrick Henry\n       </a>\n       \'s famous "\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Give_me_liberty_or_give_me_death" title="Give me liberty or give me death">\n        Give me liberty or give me death\n       </a>\n       " speech, and the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Edgar_Allan_Poe_Museum_(Richmond)" title="Edgar Allan Poe Museum (Richmond)">\n        Edgar Allan Poe Museum\n       </a>\n       , features many of his writings and other artifacts of his life, particularly when he lived in the city as a child, a student, and a successful writer. The\n       <a href="/wiki/John_Marshall" title="John Marshall">\n        John Marshall\n       </a>\n       House, the home of the former\n       <a href="/wiki/Chief_Justice_of_the_United_States" title="Chief Justice of the United States">\n        Chief Justice of the United States\n       </a>\n       , is also located downtown and features many of his writings and objects from his life.\n       <a href="/wiki/Hollywood_Cemetery_(Richmond,_Virginia)" title="Hollywood Cemetery (Richmond, Virginia)">\n        Hollywood Cemetery\n       </a>\n       is the burial grounds of two\n       <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_United_States" title="President of the United States">\n        U.S. Presidents\n       </a>\n       as well as many Civil War officers and soldiers.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The city is home to many monuments and memorials, most notably those along\n       <a href="/wiki/Monument_Avenue" title="Monument Avenue">\n        Monument Avenue\n       </a>\n       . Other monuments include the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/A.P._Hill" title="A.P. Hill">\n        A.P. Hill\n       </a>\n       monument, the\n       <a href="/wiki/Bill_Robinson" title="Bill Robinson">\n        Bill "Bojangles" Robinson\n       </a>\n       monument in Jackson Ward, the\n       <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Columbus" title="Christopher Columbus">\n        Christopher Columbus\n       </a>\n       monument near Byrd Park. Located near Byrd Park is the famous\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/World_War_I_Memorial_Carillon" title="World War I Memorial Carillon">\n        World War I Memorial Carillon\n       </a>\n       , a 56-bell\n       <a href="/wiki/Carillon" title="Carillon">\n        carillon\n       </a>\n       tower. Dedicated in 1956, the\n       <a href="/wiki/Virginia_War_Memorial" title="Virginia War Memorial">\n        Virginia War Memorial\n       </a>\n       is located on Belvedere overlooking the river, and is a monument to Virginians who died in battle in World War II, the\n       <a href="/wiki/Korean_War" title="Korean War">\n        Korean War\n       </a>\n       , the\n       <a href="/wiki/Vietnam_War" title="Vietnam War">\n        Vietnam War\n       </a>\n       , the\n       <a href="/wiki/Gulf_War" title="Gulf War">\n        Gulf War\n       </a>\n       , the\n       <a href="/wiki/War_in_Afghanistan_(2001%E2%80%93present)" title="War in Afghanistan (2001\xe2\x80\x93present)">\n        War in Afghanistan\n       </a>\n       , and the\n       <a href="/wiki/Iraq_War" title="Iraq War">\n        Iraq War\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/Agecroft_Hall" title="Agecroft Hall">\n        Agecroft Hall\n       </a>\n       is a\n       <a href="/wiki/Tudor_period" title="Tudor period">\n        Tudor\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/Manor_house" title="Manor house">\n        manor house\n       </a>\n       and estate located on the James River in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Windsor_Farms" title="Windsor Farms">\n        Windsor Farms\n       </a>\n       neighborhood of Richmond. The manor house was built in the late 15th century, and was originally located in the Agecroft area of\n       <a href="/wiki/Pendlebury" title="Pendlebury">\n        Pendlebury\n       </a>\n       , in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Historic_counties_of_England" title="Historic counties of England">\n        historic county\n       </a>\n       of\n       <a href="/wiki/Lancashire" title="Lancashire">\n        Lancashire\n       </a>\n       in\n       <a href="/wiki/England" title="England">\n        England\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Visual_and_performing_arts">\n        Visual and performing arts\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Richmond,_Virginia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Visual and performing arts">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       Richmond has a significant arts community, some of which is contained in formal public-supported venues, and some of which is more\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/DIY" title="DIY">\n        DIY\n       </a>\n       , such as local privately owned galleries, and private music venues, nonprofit arts organizations, or organic and venueless arts movements (e.g., house shows,\n       <a href="/wiki/Street_performance" title="Street performance">\n        busking\n       </a>\n       , itinerant folk shows). This has led to tensions, as the city Richmond City levied an "admissions tax" to fund large arts projects like\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/CentreStage" title="CentreStage">\n        CentreStage\n       </a>\n       , leading to criticism that it is funding civic initiatives on the backs of the organic local culture.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103">\n        <a href="#cite_note-103">\n         [100]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Traditional Virginian folk music, including\n       <a href="/wiki/Blues" title="Blues">\n        blues\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Country_music" title="Country music">\n        country\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Bluegrass_music" title="Bluegrass music">\n        bluegrass\n       </a>\n       are also notably present, and play a large part in the annual Richmond Folk Festival. The following is a list of the more formal arts establishments (Companies, theaters, galleries, and other large venues) in Richmond. Richmond is also the home and birthplace of famous metal act\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/GWAR" title="GWAR">\n        GWAR\n       </a>\n       . This is a fact members of the band consistently allude to with pride. GWAR is run by an art collective known as Slavepit Incorporated, which has over the years involved hundreds of Richmond locals.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104">\n        <a href="#cite_note-104">\n         [101]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Murals">\n        Murals\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Richmond,_Virginia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Murals">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <p>\n       As of 2015 a variety of murals from internationally recognized\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Street_artists" title="Street artists">\n        street artists\n       </a>\n       have appeared throughout the city as a result of the efforts of\n       <a href="/wiki/Art_Whino" title="Art Whino">\n        Art Whino\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/RVA_Magazine" title="RVA Magazine">\n        RVA Magazine\n       </a>\n       with The Richmond Mural Project and the RVA Street Art Festival.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105">\n        <a href="#cite_note-105">\n         [102]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Artists who have produced work in the city as a result of these festivals include\n       <a href="/wiki/ROA_(artist)" title="ROA (artist)">\n        ROA\n       </a>\n       , Pixel Pancho,\n       <a href="/wiki/Gaia_(artist)" title="Gaia (artist)">\n        Gaia\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Aryz&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Aryz (page does not exist)">\n        Aryz\n       </a>\n       , Alexis Diaz, Ever Siempre, Jaz, 2501, Natalia Rak, Pose MSK, Vizie,\n       <a href="/wiki/Jeff_Soto" title="Jeff Soto">\n        Jeff Soto\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Mark_Jenkins_(artist)" title="Mark Jenkins (artist)">\n        Mark Jenkins\n       </a>\n       , Etam Cru- and local artists Hamilton Glass, Nils Westergard, El Kamino, Nico Cathcart,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106">\n        <a href="#cite_note-106">\n         [103]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and Ed Trask. Both festivals are expected to continue this year with artists such as\n       <a href="/wiki/Ron_English_(artist)" title="Ron English (artist)">\n        Ron English\n       </a>\n       slated to produce work.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107">\n        <a href="#cite_note-107">\n         [104]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Professional_performing_companies">\n        Professional performing companies\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Richmond,_Virginia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Professional performing companies">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <p>\n       From earliest days, Virginia, and Richmond in particular, have welcomed live theatrical performances. From\n       <a href="/wiki/Lewis_Hallam" title="Lewis Hallam">\n        Lewis Hallam\n       </a>\n       \'s early productions of Shakespeare in Williamsburg, the focus shifted to Richmond\'s antebellum prominence as a main colonial and early 19th century performance venue for such celebrated American and English actors as William Macready, Edwin Forrest,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108">\n        <a href="#cite_note-108">\n         [105]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and the Booth family. In the 20th century, Richmonders\' love of theater continued with many amateur troupes and regular touring professional productions. In the 1960s a small renaissance or golden age accompanied the growth of professional dinner theaters and the fostering of theater by the Virginia Museum, reaching a peak in the 1970s with the establishment of a resident Equity company at the Virginia Museum Theater (now the Leslie Cheek) and the birth of Theatre IV, a company that continues to this day under the name Virginia Repertory Theatre.\n      </p>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Repertory_Theatre" title="Virginia Repertory Theatre">\n         Virginia Repertory Theatre\n        </a>\n        is Central Virginia\'s largest professional theatre organization. It was created in 2012 when Barksdale Theatre and Theatre IV, which had shared one staff for over a decade, merged to become one company. With an annual budget of over $5 million, the theatre employs over 240 artists each year, presenting a season at the November Theatre and Theatre Gym at Virginia Rep Center, as well as productions at the Hanover Tavern and The Children\'s Theatre in The Shops at Willow Lawn. The historic November Theatre opened in 1911 as the Empire Theatre, offering stock and vaudeville performances. In 1915 it changed its name from the Empire to the Strand and continued under that name until damaged by fire in 1927. It reopened in 1933 as the \xe2\x80\x9cBooker T,\xe2\x80\x9d and served as the leading black movie house for many years when Richmond was segregated. It closed in 1974 and was idle until real estate developer Mitchell Kambis rescued and renovated it. Kambis restored the Empire name and in 1979 leased it to Keith Fowler, artistic director of the American Revels Company. Revels restored live professional theater to downtown Richmond. Revels was succeeded by Theatre IV in 1984. On its 100th anniversary in 2011 the theatre was further restored when Sara Belle and Neil November made a $2 million gift to Theatre IV and Barksdale.[1] The November now serves as Virginia Rep\xe2\x80\x99s headquarters and home and anchors the Arts District. It is currently under the leadership of Artistic Director Bruce Miller and Managing Director Phil Whiteway.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109">\n         <a href="#cite_note-109">\n          [106]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Richmond_Ballet" title="Richmond Ballet">\n         Richmond Ballet\n        </a>\n        , founded in 1957.\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Richmond_Triangle_Players&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Richmond Triangle Players (page does not exist)">\n         Richmond Triangle Players\n        </a>\n        , founded in 1993, delivers theater programs exploring themes of equality, identity, affection and family across sexual orientation and gender spectrums.\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Richmond_Symphony" title="Richmond Symphony">\n         Richmond Symphony\n        </a>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Opera" title="Virginia Opera">\n         Virginia Opera\n        </a>\n        , the Official Opera Company of the Commonwealth of Virginia, founded in 1974. Presents eight mainstage performances every year at the\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Carpenter_Theater" title="Carpenter Theater">\n         Carpenter Theater\n        </a>\n        .\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Other_venues_and_companies">\n        Other venues and companies\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Richmond,_Virginia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Other venues and companies">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Carpenter_Theatre_Richmond_Va.JPG">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2560" data-file-width="1920" height="293" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Carpenter_Theatre_Richmond_Va.JPG/220px-Carpenter_Theatre_Richmond_Va.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Carpenter_Theatre_Richmond_Va.JPG/330px-Carpenter_Theatre_Richmond_Va.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Carpenter_Theatre_Richmond_Va.JPG/440px-Carpenter_Theatre_Richmond_Va.JPG 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Carpenter_Theatre_Richmond_Va.JPG" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         The Carpenter Theatre\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Other venues and companies include:\n      </p>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        The\n        <a href="/wiki/Altria_Theater" title="Altria Theater">\n         Altria Theater\n        </a>\n        , the city-owned\n        <a href="/wiki/Opera_house" title="Opera house">\n         opera house\n        </a>\n        .\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        The\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Leslie_Cheek_Theater" title="Leslie Cheek Theater">\n         Leslie Cheek Theater\n        </a>\n        , after lying dormant for eight years, re-opened in 2011 in the heart of the Virginia Museum of Fine Arts at 200 N. Boulevard. The elegant 500-seat proscenium stage was constructed in 1955 to match then museum director Leslie Cheek\'s vision of a theater worthy of a fine arts institution.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110">\n         <a href="#cite_note-110">\n          [107]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        Operating for years as the Virginia Museum Theater (VMT),\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111">\n         <a href="#cite_note-111">\n          [108]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        it supported an amateur community theater under the direction of Robert Telford. When Cheek retired, he advised trustees on the 1969 appointment of\n        <a href="/wiki/Keith_Fowler" title="Keith Fowler">\n         Keith Fowler\n        </a>\n        as head of the theater arts division and artistic director of VMT. Fowler led the theater to become the city\'s first resident\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Actors_Equity" title="Actors Equity">\n         Actors Equity\n        </a>\n        \\\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/LORT" title="LORT">\n         LORT\n        </a>\n        theater, adding major foreign authors and the premieres of new American works to the repertory. Under his leadership VMT reached a "golden age," gaining international recognition\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112">\n         <a href="#cite_note-112">\n          [109]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        and more than doubling its subscription base. Successive artistic administrations changed the name of the theater to "TheatreVirginia." Deficits caused TheatreVirginia to close its doors in 2002.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113">\n         <a href="#cite_note-113">\n          [110]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        Now, renovated and renamed for its founder, the Leslie Cheek is restoring live performance to VMFA and, while no longer supporting a resident company, it is available for special theatrical and performance events.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114">\n         <a href="#cite_note-114">\n          [111]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        The\n        <a href="/wiki/National_Theater_(Richmond,_Virginia)" title="National Theater (Richmond, Virginia)">\n         National Theater\n        </a>\n        is Richmond\'s premier music venue. It holds 1500 people and has shows regularly throughout the week. It opened winter of 2007 and was built in 1923. It features a state-of-the-art V-DOSC sound system, only the sixth installed in the country and only the third installed on the East Coast.\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Visual_Arts_Center_of_Richmond" title="Visual Arts Center of Richmond">\n         Visual Arts Center of Richmond\n        </a>\n        , a not-for-profit organization that is one of the largest nongovernmental arts learning centers in the state of\n        <a href="/wiki/Virginia" title="Virginia">\n         Virginia\n        </a>\n        , founded in 1963. Serves 28,000 individuals annually.\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Richmond CenterStage, a performing arts center that opened in Downtown Richmond in 2009 as part of an expansion of earlier facilities. The complex includes a renovation of the 1,700-seat\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Carpenter_Theater" title="Carpenter Theater">\n         Carpenter Theater\n        </a>\n        and construction of a new multipurpose hall, community playhouse, and arts education center in the location of the old Thalhimers department store.\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        The\n        <a href="/wiki/Byrd_Theatre" title="Byrd Theatre">\n         Byrd Theatre\n        </a>\n        in\n        <a href="/wiki/Carytown,_Richmond,_Virginia" title="Carytown, Richmond, Virginia">\n         Carytown\n        </a>\n        , a\n        <a href="/wiki/Movie_palace" title="Movie palace">\n         movie palace\n        </a>\n        from the 1920s that features second-run movies, as well as the\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/French_Film_Festival" title="French Film Festival">\n         French Film Festival\n        </a>\n        .\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Commonwealth_University" title="Virginia Commonwealth University">\n         Virginia Commonwealth University\n        </a>\n        School of the Arts, consistently ranked as one of the best in the nation.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115">\n         <a href="#cite_note-115">\n          [112]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dogwood_Dell" title="Dogwood Dell">\n         Dogwood Dell\n        </a>\n        , an amphitheatre in\n        <a href="/wiki/Byrd_Park" title="Byrd Park">\n         Byrd Park\n        </a>\n        , where the Richmond Department of Recreation and Parks presents an annual Festival of the Arts.\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/SPARC" title="SPARC">\n         SPARC\n        </a>\n        (School of the Performing Arts in the Richmond Community). SPARC was founded in 1981, and trained children to become "triple threats", meaning they were equally versed in singing, acting, and dancing. SPARC has become the largest community-based theater arts education program in Virginia and it offers classes to every age group, during the summer and throughout the year.\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Classic_Amphitheatre_at_Strawberry_Hill" title="Classic Amphitheatre at Strawberry Hill">\n         Classic Amphitheatre at Strawberry Hill\n        </a>\n        , the former summer concert venue located at\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Richmond_International_Raceway" title="Richmond International Raceway">\n         Richmond International Raceway\n        </a>\n        .\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <p>\n       Commercial art galleries include Metro Space Gallery and\n       <a href="/wiki/Gallery_5" title="Gallery 5">\n        Gallery 5\n       </a>\n       in a newly designated arts district. Not-for-profit galleries include\n       <a href="/wiki/Visual_Arts_Center_of_Richmond" title="Visual Arts Center of Richmond">\n        Visual Arts Center of Richmond\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/1708_Gallery" title="1708 Gallery">\n        1708 Galleryy\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Artspace" title="Artspace">\n        Artspace\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In addition, in 2008, a new 47,000-square-foot (4,400\xc2\xa0m\n       <sup>\n        2\n       </sup>\n       ) Gay Community Center opened on the city\'s north side, which hosts meetings of many kinds, and includes a large art gallery space.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Literary_arts">\n        Literary arts\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Richmond,_Virginia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Literary arts">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       Richmond has long been a hub for literature and writers.\n       <a href="/wiki/Edgar_Allan_Poe" title="Edgar Allan Poe">\n        Edgar Allan Poe\n       </a>\n       was a child in the city, and the town\'s oldest stone house is now a museum to his life and works.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116">\n        <a href="#cite_note-116">\n         [113]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <i>\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Southern_Literary_Messenger" title="The Southern Literary Messenger">\n         The Southern Literary Messenger\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       , which included his writing, is just one of many notable publications that began in Richmond. Other noteworthy authors who have called Richmond home include Pulitzer-winning\n       <a href="/wiki/Ellen_Glasgow" title="Ellen Glasgow">\n        Ellen Glasgow\n       </a>\n       , controversial figure\n       <a href="/wiki/James_Branch_Cabell" title="James Branch Cabell">\n        James Branch Cabell\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Meg_Medina" title="Meg Medina">\n        Meg Medina\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Dean_King" title="Dean King">\n        Dean King\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/David_L._Robbins_(Virginia_writer)" title="David L. Robbins (Virginia writer)">\n        David L. Robbins\n       </a>\n       , and MacArthur Fellow\n       <a href="/wiki/Paule_Marshall" title="Paule Marshall">\n        Paule Marshall\n       </a>\n       .\n       <a href="/wiki/Tom_Wolfe" title="Tom Wolfe">\n        Tom Wolfe\n       </a>\n       was born in Richmond, as was\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Breaking_Bad" title="Breaking Bad">\n         Breaking Bad\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       creator\n       <a href="/wiki/Vince_Gilligan" title="Vince Gilligan">\n        Vince Gilligan\n       </a>\n       .\n       <a href="/wiki/David_Baldacci" title="David Baldacci">\n        David Baldacci\n       </a>\n       graduated from\n       <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Commonwealth_University" title="Virginia Commonwealth University">\n        Virginia Commonwealth University\n       </a>\n       , where the creative writing faculty has included Marshall,\n       <a href="/wiki/Claudia_Emerson" title="Claudia Emerson">\n        Claudia Emerson\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Kathleen_Graber" title="Kathleen Graber">\n        Kathleen Graber\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/T._R._Hummer" title="T. R. Hummer">\n        T. R. Hummer\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Dave_Smith_(poet)" title="Dave Smith (poet)">\n        Dave Smith\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/David_Wojahn" title="David Wojahn">\n        David Wojahn\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Susann_Cokal" title="Susann Cokal">\n        Susann Cokal\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Thomas_De_Haven&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Thomas De Haven (page does not exist)">\n        Thomas De Haven\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Larry_Levis.&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Larry Levis. (page does not exist)">\n        Larry Levis.\n       </a>\n       Notable graduates include\n       <a href="/wiki/Sheri_Reynolds" title="Sheri Reynolds">\n        Sheri Reynolds\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Jon_Pineda" title="Jon Pineda">\n        Jon Pineda\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Anna_Journey" title="Anna Journey">\n        Anna Journey\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Joshua_Poteat.&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Joshua Poteat. (page does not exist)">\n        Joshua Poteat.\n       </a>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-english.vcu.edu_117-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-english.vcu.edu-117">\n         [114]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       A community-based organization called\n       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=James_River_Writers&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="James River Writers (page does not exist)">\n        James River Writers\n       </a>\n       serves the greater Richmond area; it sponsors many programs for writers at all stages of their careers and puts on an annual writers\' conference that draws attendees from miles away.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-english.vcu.edu_117-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-english.vcu.edu-117">\n         [114]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Architecture">\n        Architecture\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Richmond,_Virginia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Architecture">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       See also:\n       <a href="/wiki/National_Register_of_Historic_Places_listings_in_Richmond,_Virginia" title="National Register of Historic Places listings in Richmond, Virginia">\n        National Register of Historic Places listings in Richmond, Virginia\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_tallest_buildings_in_Richmond" title="List of tallest buildings in Richmond">\n        List of tallest buildings in Richmond\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tleft">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Va_Capitol.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="890" data-file-width="1112" height="176" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Va_Capitol.jpg/220px-Va_Capitol.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Va_Capitol.jpg/330px-Va_Capitol.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Va_Capitol.jpg/440px-Va_Capitol.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Va_Capitol.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Thomas Jefferson designed the\n         <a href="/wiki/Virginia_State_Capitol" title="Virginia State Capitol">\n          Virginia State Capitol\n         </a>\n         in Richmond\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Richmond is home to many significant structures, including some designed by notable architects. The city contains diverse styles, including significant examples of Georgian, Federal, Greek Revival, Neoclassical, Egyptian Revival, Romanesque Revival, Gothic Revival, Tudor Revival, Italianate, Queen Anne, Colonial Revival, Art Deco, Modernist, International, and Postmodern buildings.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Much of Richmond\'s early architecture was destroyed by the Evacuation Fire in 1865. It is estimated that 25% of all buildings in Richmond were destroyed during this fire.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118">\n        <a href="#cite_note-118">\n         [115]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Even fewer now remain due to construction and\n       <a href="/wiki/Urban_renewal" title="Urban renewal">\n        demolition\n       </a>\n       that has taken place since\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Reconstruction_era_of_the_United_States" title="Reconstruction era of the United States">\n        Reconstruction\n       </a>\n       . In spite of this, Richmond contains many historically significant buildings and districts. Buildings remain from Richmond\'s colonial period, such as the\n       <a href="/wiki/Patteson-Schutte_House" title="Patteson-Schutte House">\n        Patteson-Schutte House\n       </a>\n       and the\n       <a href="/wiki/Edgar_Allan_Poe_Museum_(Richmond,_Virginia)" title="Edgar Allan Poe Museum (Richmond, Virginia)">\n        Edgar Allan Poe Museum (Richmond, Virginia)\n       </a>\n       , both built before 1750.\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Egyptian_Building.JPG">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2448" data-file-width="3264" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Egyptian_Building.JPG/220px-Egyptian_Building.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Egyptian_Building.JPG/330px-Egyptian_Building.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Egyptian_Building.JPG/440px-Egyptian_Building.JPG 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Egyptian_Building.JPG" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <a href="/wiki/Egyptian_Building" title="Egyptian Building">\n          Egyptian Building\n         </a>\n         of the VCU School of Medicine (1845), Richmond, Virginia\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Architectural classicism is heavily represented in all districts of the city, particularly in Downtown, the Fan, and the Museum District. Several notable classical architects have designed buildings in Richmond. The Virginia State Capitol was designed by\n       <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Jefferson" title="Thomas Jefferson">\n        Thomas Jefferson\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Charles-Louis_Cl%C3%A9risseau" title="Charles-Louis Cl\xc3\xa9risseau">\n        Charles-Louis Cl\xc3\xa9risseau\n       </a>\n       in 1785. It is the second-oldest US statehouse in continuous use (after Maryland\'s) and was the first US government building built in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Neoclassical_architecture" title="Neoclassical architecture">\n        neo-classical\n       </a>\n       style of architecture, setting the trend for other state houses and the federal government buildings (including the\n       <a href="/wiki/White_House" title="White House">\n        White House\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/United_States_Capitol" title="United States Capitol">\n        The Capitol\n       </a>\n       ) in Washington, D.C.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jefferson_capital_119-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-jefferson_capital-119">\n         [116]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Robert Mills designed\n       <a href="/wiki/Monumental_Church" title="Monumental Church">\n        Monumental Church\n       </a>\n       on Broad Street. Adjoining it is the 1845\n       <a href="/wiki/Egyptian_Building" title="Egyptian Building">\n        Egyptian Building\n       </a>\n       , one of the few\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Egyptian_Revival" title="Egyptian Revival">\n        Egyptian Revival\n       </a>\n       buildings in the United States.\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tleft">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Science_Museum_-_Broad_Street_Station_(2256100684).jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1064" data-file-width="1600" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Science_Museum_-_Broad_Street_Station_%282256100684%29.jpg/220px-Science_Museum_-_Broad_Street_Station_%282256100684%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Science_Museum_-_Broad_Street_Station_%282256100684%29.jpg/330px-Science_Museum_-_Broad_Street_Station_%282256100684%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Science_Museum_-_Broad_Street_Station_%282256100684%29.jpg/440px-Science_Museum_-_Broad_Street_Station_%282256100684%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Science_Museum_-_Broad_Street_Station_(2256100684).jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         The\n         <a href="/wiki/Science_Museum_of_Virginia" title="Science Museum of Virginia">\n          Science Museum of Virginia\n         </a>\n         , housed in\n         <a href="/wiki/Broad_Street_Station_(Richmond)" title="Broad Street Station (Richmond)">\n          Broad Street Station\n         </a>\n         , designed by\n         <a href="/wiki/John_Russell_Pope" title="John Russell Pope">\n          John Russell Pope\n         </a>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The firm of\n       <a href="/wiki/John_Russell_Pope" title="John Russell Pope">\n        John Russell Pope\n       </a>\n       designed\n       <a href="/wiki/Broad_Street_Station_(Richmond)" title="Broad Street Station (Richmond)">\n        Broad Street Station\n       </a>\n       as well as\n       <a href="/wiki/Branch_House" title="Branch House">\n        Branch House\n       </a>\n       on\n       <a href="/wiki/Monument_Avenue" title="Monument Avenue">\n        Monument Avenue\n       </a>\n       , designed as a private residence in the Tudor style, now serving as the Branch Museum of Architecture and Design. Broad Street Station (or Union Station), designed in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Beaux-Arts_architecture" title="Beaux-Arts architecture">\n        Beaux-Arts\n       </a>\n       style, is no longer a functioning station but is now home to the\n       <a href="/wiki/Science_Museum_of_Virginia" title="Science Museum of Virginia">\n        Science Museum of Virginia\n       </a>\n       .\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Main_Street_Station_(Richmond)" title="Main Street Station (Richmond)">\n        Main Street Station\n       </a>\n       , designed by Wilson, Harris, and Richards, has been returned to use in its original purpose. The Jefferson Hotel and the Commonwealth Club were both designed by the classically trained Beaux-Arts architects Carr\xc3\xa8re and Hastings. Many buildings on the\n       <a href="/wiki/University_of_Richmond" title="University of Richmond">\n        University of Richmond\n       </a>\n       campus, including Jeter Hall and Ryland Hall, were designed by\n       <a href="/wiki/Ralph_Adams_Cram" title="Ralph Adams Cram">\n        Ralph Adams Cram\n       </a>\n       , most famous for his Princeton University Chapel and the Cathedral of Saint John the Divine.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Richmond\'s urban residential neighborhoods also hold particular significance to the city\'s fabric. The Fan, the Museum District, Jackson Ward, Carver, Carytown, Oregon Hill and Church Hill (among others) are largely single use town homes and mixed use or full retail/dining establishments. These districts are anchored by large streets such as Franklin Street, Cary Street, the Boulevard, and Monument Avenue. The city\'s growth in population over the last decade has been concentrated in these areas.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Among Richmond\'s most interesting architectural features is its\n       <a href="/wiki/Cast-iron_architecture" title="Cast-iron architecture">\n        Cast-iron architecture\n       </a>\n       . Second only to\n       <a href="/wiki/New_Orleans" title="New Orleans">\n        New Orleans\n       </a>\n       in its concentration of cast iron work, the city is home to a unique collection of cast iron porches, balconies, fences, and finials. Richmond\'s position as a center of iron production helped to fuel its popularity within the city. At the height of production in the 1890, 25 foundries operated in the city employing nearly 3,500 metal workers. This number is seven times the number of general construction workers being employed in Richmond at the time which illustrates the importance of its iron exports.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120">\n        <a href="#cite_note-120">\n         [117]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Porches and fences in urban neighborhoods such as Jackson Ward, Church Hill, and Monroe Ward are particularly elaborate, often featuring ornate iron casts never replicated outside of Richmond. In some cases cast were made for a single residential or commercial application.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Richmond is home to several notable instances of various styles of modernism.\n       <a href="/wiki/Minoru_Yamasaki" title="Minoru Yamasaki">\n        Minoru Yamasaki\n       </a>\n       designed the Federal Reserve Building which dominates the downtown skyline. The\n       <a href="/wiki/Architectural_firm" title="Architectural firm">\n        architectural firm\n       </a>\n       of\n       <a href="/wiki/Skidmore,_Owings_%26_Merrill" title="Skidmore, Owings &amp; Merrill">\n        Skidmore, Owings &amp; Merrill\n       </a>\n       has designed two buildings: the\n       <a href="/wiki/Library_of_Virginia" title="Library of Virginia">\n        Library of Virginia\n       </a>\n       and the General Assembly Offices at the Eighth and Main Building.\n       <a href="/wiki/Philip_Johnson" title="Philip Johnson">\n        Philip Johnson\n       </a>\n       designed the\n       <a href="/wiki/WRVA_Building" title="WRVA Building">\n        WRVA Building\n       </a>\n       . The\n       <a href="/wiki/Richard_Neutra" title="Richard Neutra">\n        Richard Neutra\n       </a>\n       -designed\n       <a href="/wiki/Rice_House_(Richmond,_Virginia)" title="Rice House (Richmond, Virginia)">\n        Rice House\n       </a>\n       , a residence on a private island on the James River, remains Richmond\'s only true International Style home. The W.G. Harris residence in Richmond was designed by famed early modern architect and member of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Harvard_Five" title="Harvard Five">\n        Harvard Five\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121">\n        <a href="#cite_note-121">\n         [118]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <a href="/wiki/Landis_Gores" title="Landis Gores">\n        Landis Gores\n       </a>\n       . Other notable architects to have worked in the city include Rick Mather,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/I.M._Pei" title="I.M. Pei">\n        I.M. Pei\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Gordon_Bunshaft" title="Gordon Bunshaft">\n        Gordon Bunshaft\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       VCU is currently raising funds for a new Institute of Contemporary Arts designed by\n       <a href="/wiki/Steven_Holl" title="Steven Holl">\n        Steven Holl\n       </a>\n       . The ICA is funded by private donors and is scheduled to open in late 2017.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Historic_districts">\n        Historic districts\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Richmond,_Virginia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Historic districts">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       Richmond\'s City Code provides for the creation of old and historic districts so as to "recognize and protect the historic, architectural, cultural, and artistic heritage of the City."\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122">\n        <a href="#cite_note-122">\n         [119]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Pursuant to that authority, the city has designated 45 districts throughout the city.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123">\n        <a href="#cite_note-123">\n         [120]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The majority of these districts are also listed in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Landmarks_Register" title="Virginia Landmarks Register">\n        Virginia Landmarks Register\n       </a>\n       ("VLR") and the\n       <a href="/wiki/National_Register_of_Historic_Places" title="National Register of Historic Places">\n        National Register of Historic Places\n       </a>\n       ("NRHP").\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Fifteen of the districts represent broad sections of the city:\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124">\n        <a href="#cite_note-124">\n         [121]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <table class="wikitable">\n       <tr>\n        <th>\n         Historic District\n        </th>\n        <th>\n    <td>\n         <a href="/wiki/St._Peter%27s_Church_(Richmond,_Virginia)" title="St. Peter\'s Church (Richmond, Virginia)">\n          St. Peter\'s Catholic Church\n         </a>\n         (800 East  <tr>\n        <td>\n         <a href="/wiki/Second_Presbyterian_Church_(Richmond,_Virginia)" title="Second Presbyterian Church (Richmond, Virginia)">\n          Second Presbyterian Church\n 1968\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         <a class="external text" href="http://www.dhr.virginia.gov/registers/Cities/Richmond/127-0020_Wickham-Valentine_House_1969_Final_Nomination.pdf"    </a>\n         (4301 Sulgrave Road)\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         1989\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         <a class="external text" <td>\n         1975\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         <a class="external text" href="http://www.dhr.virginia.gov/registers/Cities/Richmond/127-0141_Wilton_1976_Final_Nomination.pdf" </table>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Food">\n        Food\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Richmond,_Virginia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Food">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       Richmond has been recognized in recent years for being a "\n       <a href="/wiki/Foodie" title="Foodie">\n        foodie\n       </a>\n       city", particularly for its modern renditions of traditional\n       <a href="/wiki/Cuisine_of_the_Southern_United_States" title="Cuisine of the Southern United States">\n        southern cuisine\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RTJ_Foodie_126-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-RTJ_Foodie-126">\n         [123]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CNN_foodie_127-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-CNN_foodie-127">\n         [124]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USNews_Foodie_128-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-USNews_Foodie-128">\n         [125]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The city also claims the invention of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Sailor_sandwich" title="Sailor sandwich">\n        sailor sandwich\n       </a>\n       , which includes\n       <a href="/wiki/Pastrami" title="Pastrami">\n        pastrami\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Knockwurst" title="Knockwurst">\n        knockwurst\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Swiss_cheese" title="Swiss cheese">\n        Swiss cheese\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Mustard_(condiment)" title="Mustard (condiment)">\n        mustard\n       </a>\n       on\n       <a href="/wiki/Rye_bread" title="Rye bread">\n        rye bread\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Imajo_129-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Imajo-129">\n         [126]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Richmond is also where, in 1935, canned beer was made commercially available for the first time.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130">\n        <a href="#cite_note-130">\n         [127]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Parks_and_outdoor_recreation">\n        Parks and outdoor recreation\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Richmond,_Virginia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Parks and outdoor recreation">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Botanicalgarden.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="254" data-file-width="395" height="141" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Botanicalgarden.jpg/220px-Botanicalgarden.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Botanicalgarden.jpg/330px-Botanicalgarden.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/1/1a/Botanicalgarden.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Botanicalgarden.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <a href="/wiki/Lewis_Ginter_Botanical_Garden" title="Lewis Ginter Botanical Garden">\n          Lewis Ginter Botanical Garden\n         </a>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The city operates one of the oldest municipal park systems in the country. The park system began when the city council voted in 1851 to acquire 7.5 acres (30,000\xc2\xa0m\n       <sup>\n        2\n       </sup>\n       ), now known as\n       <a href="/wiki/Monroe_Park" title="Monroe Park">\n        Monroe Park\n       </a>\n       . Today, Monroe Park sits adjacent to the\n       <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Commonwealth_University" title="Virginia Commonwealth University">\n        Virginia Commonwealth University\n       </a>\n       campus and is one of more than 40 parks comprising a total of more than 1,500 acres (610\xc2\xa0ha).\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Several parks are located along the James River, and the James River Parks System offers bike trails, hiking and nature trails, and many scenic overlooks along the river\'s route through the city.\n       <a class="external free" href="https://www.trailforks.com/region/james-river-park-system/" rel="nofollow">\n        https://www.trailforks.com/region/james-river-park-system/\n       </a>\n       The trails are used as part of the Xterra East Championship course for both the running and mountain biking portions of the off-road triathlon.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131">\n        <a href="#cite_note-131">\n         [128]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       There are also parks on two major islands in the river:\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Belle_Isle_(Virginia)" title="Belle Isle (Virginia)">\n        Belle Isle\n       </a>\n       and Brown\'s Island. Belle Isle, at various former times a Powhatan fishing village, colonial-era horse race track, and Civil War prison camp, is the larger of the two, and contains many bike trails as well as a small cliff that is used for\n       <a href="/wiki/Rock_climbing" title="Rock climbing">\n        rock climbing\n       </a>\n       instruction. One can walk the island and still see many of the remains of the Civil War prison camp, such as an arms storage room and a gun emplacement that was used to quell prisoner riots. Brown\'s Island is a smaller island and a popular venue of a large number of free outdoor concerts and festivals in the spring and summer, such as the weekly Friday Cheers concert series or the James River Beer and Seafood Festival.\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tleft">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:MaymontPark_JapaneseGarden.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="518" data-file-width="650" height="175" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/MaymontPark_JapaneseGarden.jpg/220px-MaymontPark_JapaneseGarden.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/MaymontPark_JapaneseGarden.jpg/330px-MaymontPark_JapaneseGarden.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/MaymontPark_JapaneseGarden.jpg/440px-MaymontPark_JapaneseGarden.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:MaymontPark_JapaneseGarden.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Japanese Garden at\n         <a href="/wiki/Maymont" title="Maymont">\n          Maymont\n         </a>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Two other major parks in the city along the river are\n       <a href="/wiki/Byrd_Park" title="Byrd Park">\n        Byrd Park\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Maymont" title="Maymont">\n        Maymont\n       </a>\n       , located near the Fan District. Byrd Park features a one-mile (1.6\xc2\xa0km) running track, with exercise stops, a public\n       <a href="/wiki/Dog_park" title="Dog park">\n        dog park\n       </a>\n       , and a number of small lakes for small boats, as well as two monuments, Buddha house, and an amphitheatre. Prominently featured in the park is the\n       <a href="/wiki/Carillon" title="Carillon">\n        World War I Memorial Carillon\n       </a>\n       , built in 1926 as a memorial to those that died in the war. Maymont, located adjacent to Byrd Park, is a 100-acre (40\xc2\xa0ha)\n       <a href="/wiki/Victorian_architecture" title="Victorian architecture">\n        Victorian\n       </a>\n       estate with a museum, formal gardens, native wildlife exhibits, nature center,\n       <a href="/wiki/Carriage" title="Carriage">\n        carriage\n       </a>\n       collection, and children\'s farm. Other parks in the city include\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Joseph_Bryan_Park_Azalea_Garden" title="Joseph Bryan Park Azalea Garden">\n        Joseph Bryan Park Azalea Garden\n       </a>\n       , Forest Hill Park (former site of the Forest Hill Amusement Park),\n       <a href="/wiki/Chimborazo_Park" title="Chimborazo Park">\n        Chimborazo Park\n       </a>\n       (site of the National Battlefield Headquarters), among others.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The James River itself through Richmond is renowned as one of the best in the country for urban white-water rafting/canoeing/kayaking. Several rafting companies offer complete services. There are also several easily accessed riverside areas within the city limits for rock-hopping, swimming, and picnicking.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/Lewis_Ginter_Botanical_Garden" title="Lewis Ginter Botanical Garden">\n        Lewis Ginter Botanical Garden\n       </a>\n       is located adjacent to the city in Henrico County. Founded in 1984, Lewis Ginter Botanical Garden is located on 80 acres (320,000\xc2\xa0m\n       <sup>\n        2\n       </sup>\n       ) and features a glass conservatory, a rose garden, a healing garden, and an accessible-to-all children\'s garden. The Garden is a public place for the display and scientific study of plants. Lewis Ginter Botanical Garden is one of only two independent public botanical gardens in Virginia and is designated a state botanical garden.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132">\n        <a href="#cite_note-132">\n         [129]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Several\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Theme_park" title="Theme park">\n        theme parks\n       </a>\n       are also located near the city, including\n       <a href="/wiki/Kings_Dominion" title="Kings Dominion">\n        Kings Dominion\n       </a>\n       to the north, and\n       <a href="/wiki/Busch_Gardens" title="Busch Gardens">\n        Busch Gardens\n       </a>\n       to the east, near\n       <a href="/wiki/Williamsburg,_Virginia" title="Williamsburg, Virginia">\n        Williamsburg\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">\n        Sports\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Richmond,_Virginia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Sports">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Sports_in_Richmond,_Virginia" title="Sports in Richmond, Virginia">\n        Sports in Richmond, Virginia\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Richmond is not home to any major league professional sports teams, but since 2013, the\n       <a href="/wiki/Washington_Redskins" title="Washington Redskins">\n        Washington Redskins\n       </a>\n       of the\n       <a href="/wiki/National_Football_League" title="National Football League">\n        National Football League\n       </a>\n       have held their\n       <a href="/wiki/Training_camp_(National_Football_League)" title="Training camp (National Football League)">\n        summer training camp\n       </a>\n       in the city.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Redskins_133-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Redskins-133">\n         [130]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       There are also several\n       <a href="/wiki/Minor_league" title="Minor league">\n        minor league\n       </a>\n       sports in the city, including the\n       <a href="/wiki/Richmond_Kickers" title="Richmond Kickers">\n        Richmond Kickers\n       </a>\n       of the\n       <a href="/wiki/United_Soccer_League" title="United Soccer League">\n        United Soccer League\n       </a>\n       (joint second tier of\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/American_soccer_pyramid" title="American soccer pyramid">\n        American soccer\n       </a>\n       ) and the\n       <a href="/wiki/Richmond_Flying_Squirrels" title="Richmond Flying Squirrels">\n        Richmond Flying Squirrels\n       </a>\n       of the Class AA\n       <a href="/wiki/Eastern_League_(baseball)" title="Eastern League (baseball)">\n        Eastern League\n       </a>\n       of\n       <a href="/wiki/Minor_League_Baseball" title="Minor League Baseball">\n        Minor League Baseball\n       </a>\n       (an affiliate of the\n       <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco_Giants" title="San Francisco Giants">\n        San Francisco Giants\n       </a>\n       ).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kickers_134-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-kickers-134">\n         [131]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-squirrels_135-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-squirrels-135">\n         [132]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The Kickers began playing in Richmond in 1993, and currently play at\n       <a href="/wiki/City_Stadium_(Richmond)" title="City Stadium (Richmond)">\n        City Stadium\n       </a>\n       . The Squirrels opened their first season at\n       <a href="/wiki/The_Diamond_(Richmond,_Virginia)" title="The Diamond (Richmond, Virginia)">\n        The Diamond\n       </a>\n       on April 15, 2010.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136">\n        <a href="#cite_note-136">\n         [133]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       From 1966 through 2008, the city was home to the\n       <a href="/wiki/Richmond_Braves" title="Richmond Braves">\n        Richmond Braves\n       </a>\n       , a AAA affiliate of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Atlanta_Braves" title="Atlanta Braves">\n        Atlanta Braves\n       </a>\n       of\n       <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball" title="Major League Baseball">\n        Major League Baseball\n       </a>\n       , until the franchise relocated to\n       <a href="/wiki/Georgia_(U.S._state)" title="Georgia (U.S. state)">\n        Georgia\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137">\n        <a href="#cite_note-137">\n         [134]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       It is also the home to the\n       <a href="/wiki/Richmond_Black_Widows" title="Richmond Black Widows">\n        Richmond Black Widows\n       </a>\n       , the city\'s first women\'s football team, founded in 2015 by\n       <a href="/wiki/Sarah_Schkeeper" title="Sarah Schkeeper">\n        Sarah Schkeeper\n       </a>\n       . They are a part of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Women%27s_Football_Alliance" title="Women\'s Football Alliance">\n        Women\'s Football Alliance\n       </a>\n       . Their game season begins in April, with preseason beginning in January.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Another significant sports venue is the 6,000-seat\n       <a href="/wiki/Arthur_Ashe_Athletic_Center" title="Arthur Ashe Athletic Center">\n        Arthur Ashe Athletic Center\n       </a>\n       , a multi-purpose arena named for tennis great and Richmond resident\n       <a href="/wiki/Arthur_Ashe" title="Arthur Ashe">\n        Arthur Ashe\n       </a>\n       . This facility hosts a variety of local sporting events, concerts, and other activities. As the home of Arthur Ashe, the sport of\n       <a href="/wiki/Tennis" title="Tennis">\n        tennis\n       </a>\n       is also popular in Richmond, and in 2010, the\n       <a href="/wiki/United_States_Tennis_Association" title="United States Tennis Association">\n        United States Tennis Association\n       </a>\n       named Richmond as the third "Best Tennis Town", behind\n       <a href="/wiki/Charleston,_South_Carolina" title="Charleston, South Carolina">\n        Charleston, South Carolina\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Atlanta,_Georgia" title="Atlanta, Georgia">\n        Atlanta, Georgia\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USTA_138-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-USTA-138">\n         [135]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Auto racing is also popular in the area. The\n       <a href="/wiki/Richmond_Raceway" title="Richmond Raceway">\n        Richmond Raceway\n       </a>\n       (RR) has hosted\n       <a href="/wiki/Monster_Energy" title="Monster Energy">\n        Monster Energy\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/NASCAR" title="NASCAR">\n        NASCAR\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/Monster_Energy_NASCAR_Cup_Series" title="Monster Energy NASCAR Cup Series">\n        Cup\n       </a>\n       races since 1953, as well as the Capital City 400 from 1962 \xe2\x88\x92 1980.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RIR_139-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-RIR-139">\n         [136]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       RIR also hosted IndyCar\'s Suntrust Indy Challenge from 2001 \xe2\x88\x92 2009. Another track,\n       <a href="/wiki/Southside_Speedway" title="Southside Speedway">\n        Southside Speedway\n       </a>\n       , has operated since 1959 and sits just southwest of Richmond in\n       <a href="/wiki/Chesterfield_County,_Virginia" title="Chesterfield County, Virginia">\n        Chesterfield County\n       </a>\n       . This .333-mile (0.536\xc2\xa0km) oval short-track has become known as the "Toughest Track in the South" and "The Action Track", and features weekly stock car racing on Friday nights.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Southside_Speedway_140-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Southside_Speedway-140">\n         [137]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Southside Speedway has acted as the breeding grounds for many past NASCAR legends including\n       <a href="/wiki/Richard_Petty" title="Richard Petty">\n        Richard Petty\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Bobby_Allison" title="Bobby Allison">\n        Bobby Allison\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Darrell_Waltrip" title="Darrell Waltrip">\n        Darrell Waltrip\n       </a>\n       , and claims to be the home track of NASCAR superstar\n       <a href="/wiki/Denny_Hamlin" title="Denny Hamlin">\n        Denny Hamlin\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Netherland_Tom_141-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Netherland_Tom-141">\n         [138]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Brockwell_Kent_142-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Brockwell_Kent-142">\n         [139]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In 2015, Richmond hosted the\n       <a href="/wiki/2015_UCI_Road_World_Championships" title="2015 UCI Road World Championships">\n        2015 UCI Road World Championships\n       </a>\n       , which had cyclists from 76 countries and an economic impact on the\n       <a href="/wiki/Greater_Richmond_Region" title="Greater Richmond Region">\n        Greater Richmond Region\n       </a>\n       estimated to be $158.1 million, from both event staging and visitor spending.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143">\n        <a href="#cite_note-143">\n         [140]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/College_basketball" title="College basketball">\n        College basketball\n       </a>\n       has also had recent success with the\n       <a href="/wiki/Richmond_Spiders" title="Richmond Spiders">\n        Richmond Spiders\n       </a>\n       and the\n       <a href="/wiki/VCU_Rams" title="VCU Rams">\n        VCU Rams\n       </a>\n       , both of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_10_Conference" title="Atlantic 10 Conference">\n        Atlantic 10 Conference\n       </a>\n       . The Spiders\' men\'s and women\'s teams play at\n       <a href="/wiki/Robins_Center" title="Robins Center">\n        Robins Center\n       </a>\n       and the Rams\' men\'s and women\'s teams play at the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Stuart_C._Siegel_Center" title="Stuart C. Siegel Center">\n        Stuart C. Siegel Center\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Media">\n        Media\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Richmond,_Virginia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Media">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation">\n       <tr>\n        <td class="mbox-image">\n         <div style="width:52px">\n          <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg">\n           <img alt="" data-file-height="399" data-file-width="512" height="39" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" width="50"/>\n          </a>\n         </div>\n        </td>\n        <td class="mbox-text">\n         <div class="mbox-text-span">\n          This article\n          <b>\n           needs additional citations for\n           <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">\n            verification\n           </a>\n          </b>\n          .\n          <span class="hide-when-compact">\n           Please help\n           <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Richmond,_Virginia&amp;action=edit">\n            improve this article\n           </a>\n           by\n           <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">\n            adding citations to reliable sources\n           </a>\n           . Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.\n          </span>\n          <small>\n           <i>\n            (September 2016)\n           </i>\n          </small>\n          <small class="hide-when-compact">\n           <i>\n            (\n            <a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">\n             Learn how and when to remove this template message\n            </a>\n            )\n           </i>\n          </small>\n         </div>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Media_in_Richmond,_Virginia" title="Media in Richmond, Virginia">\n        Media in Richmond, Virginia\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Richmond_Times-Dispatch" title="Richmond Times-Dispatch">\n         Richmond Times-Dispatch\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       , the local daily newspaper in Richmond with a Sunday circulation of 120,000, is owned by BH Media, a subsidiary of Warren Buffett\'s\n       <a href="/wiki/Berkshire_Hathaway" title="Berkshire Hathaway">\n        Berkshire Hathaway\n       </a>\n       company.\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Style_Weekly" title="Style Weekly">\n         Style Weekly\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       is a standard weekly publication covering popular culture, arts, and entertainment, owned by Landmark Communications.\n       <a href="/wiki/RVA_Magazine" title="RVA Magazine">\n        RVA Magazine\n       </a>\n       is the city\'s only independent art music and culture publication, was once monthly, but is now issued quarterly. The\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Richmond_Free_Press" title="Richmond Free Press">\n         Richmond Free Press\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       and the\n       <i>\n        Voice\n       </i>\n       cover the news from an African-American perspective.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The Richmond metro area is served by many local television and radio stations. As of 2010\n       <sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;">\n        <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Richmond,_Virginia&amp;action=edit">\n         [update]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       , the Richmond-Petersburg\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Designated_market_area" title="Designated market area">\n        designated market area\n       </a>\n       (DMA) is the 58th largest in the U.S. with 553,950 homes according to Nielsen Market Research.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nielsen_144-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-nielsen-144">\n         [141]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The major network television affiliates are\n       <a href="/wiki/WTVR-TV" title="WTVR-TV">\n        WTVR-TV\n       </a>\n       6 (\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Columbia_Broadcasting_System" title="Columbia Broadcasting System">\n        CBS\n       </a>\n       ),\n       <a href="/wiki/WRIC-TV" title="WRIC-TV">\n        WRIC-TV\n       </a>\n       8 (\n       <a href="/wiki/American_Broadcasting_Company" title="American Broadcasting Company">\n        ABC\n       </a>\n       ),\n       <a href="/wiki/WWBT" title="WWBT">\n        WWBT\n       </a>\n       12 (\n       <a href="/wiki/NBC" title="NBC">\n        NBC\n       </a>\n       ),\n       <a href="/wiki/WRLH-TV" title="WRLH-TV">\n        WRLH-TV\n       </a>\n       35 (\n       <a href="/wiki/Fox_Broadcasting_Company" title="Fox Broadcasting Company">\n        Fox\n       </a>\n       ), and\n       <a href="/wiki/WUPV" title="WUPV">\n        WUPV\n       </a>\n       65 (\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_CW_Television_Network" title="The CW Television Network">\n        CW\n       </a>\n       ).\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Public_Broadcasting_Service" title="Public Broadcasting Service">\n        Public Broadcasting Service\n       </a>\n       stations include\n       <a href="/wiki/WCVE-TV" title="WCVE-TV">\n        WCVE-TV\n       </a>\n       23 and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/WCVW" title="WCVW">\n        WCVW\n       </a>\n       57. There are also a wide variety of radio stations in the Richmond area, catering to many different interests, including news,\n       <a href="/wiki/Talk_radio" title="Talk radio">\n        talk radio\n       </a>\n       , and sports, as well as an eclectic mix of musical interests.\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Government_and_politics">\n        Government and
