background:honeyDew;">\n         6.8%\n         <i>\n          917\n         </i>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td style="background:#B0CEFF">\n         <b>\n          <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election_in_Virginia,_1920" title="United States presidential election in Virginia, 1920">\n           1920\n          </a>\n         </b>\n        </td>\n        <td style="background:#FFB6B6">\n         23.0%\n         <i>\n          4,515\n         </i>\n        </td>\n        <td style="background:#B0CEFF">\n         <b>\n          75.9%\n         </b>\n         <i>\n          14,878\n         </i>\n        </td>\n        <td style="text-align:center; background:honeyDew;">\n         1.0%\n         <i>\n          202\n         </i>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td style="background:#B0CEFF">\n         <b>\n          <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election_in_Virginia,_1916" title="United States presidential election in Virginia, 1916">\n           1916\n          </a>\n         </b>\n        </td>\n        <td style="background:#FFB6B6">\n         14.6%\n         <i>\n          1,210\n         </i>\n        </td>\n        <td style="background:#B0CEFF">\n         <b>\n          84.2%\n         </b>\n         <i>\n          6,987\n         </i>\n        </td>\n        <td style="text-align:center; background:honeyDew;">\n         1.3%\n         <i>\n          106\n         </i>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td style="background:#B0CEFF">\n         <b>\n          <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election_in_Virginia,_1912" title="United States presidential election in Virginia, 1912">\n           1912\n          </a>\n         </b>\n        </td>\n        <td style="background:#FFB6B6">\n         6.1%\n         <i>\n          405\n         </i>\n        </td>\n        <td style="background:#B0CEFF">\n         <b>\n          85.0%\n         </b>\n         <i>\n          5,632\n         </i>\n        </td>\n        <td style="text-align:center; background:honeyDew;">\n         8.9%\n         <i>\n          586\n         </i>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <p>\n       Richmond city government consists of a\n       <a href="/wiki/City_council" title="City council">\n        city council\n       </a>\n       with representatives from nine districts serving in a\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Legislative" title="Legislative">\n        legislative\n       </a>\n       and oversight capacity, as well as a popularly elected, at-large mayor serving as head of the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Executive_branch" title="Executive branch">\n        executive branch\n       </a>\n       . Citizens in each of the nine districts elect one council representative each to serve a four-year term. Beginning with the November 2008 election Council terms was lengthened to 4 years. The city council elects from among its members one member to serve as Council President and one to serve as Council Vice President. The city council meets at City Hall, located at 900 E. Broad St., 2nd Floor, on the second and fourth Mondays of every month, except August.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In 1977, a federal district court ruled in favor of\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Curtis_Holt_Jr." title="Curtis Holt Jr.">\n        Curtis Holt Jr.\n       </a>\n       who had claimed the council\'s existing election process\xc2\xa0\xe2\x80\x94 an at large voting system\xc2\xa0\xe2\x80\x94 was racially biased. The verdict required the city to rebuild its council into nine distinct wards. Within the year the city council switched from majority white to majority black, reflecting the city\'s populace. This new city council elected Richmond\'s first black mayor,\n       <a href="/wiki/Henry_L._Marsh" title="Henry L. Marsh">\n        Henry L. Marsh\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In 1990 religion and politics intersected to impact the outcome of the Eighth District election in South Richmond. With the endorsements of black power brokers, black clergy and the Richmond Crusade for Voters, South Richmond residents made history, electing Reverend A. Carl Prince to the Richmond City Council. As the first African American Baptist Minister elected to the Richmond City Council, Prince\'s election paved the way for a political paradigm shift in politics that persist today. Following Prince\'s election, Reverend Gwendolyn Hedgepeth and the Reverend Leonidas Young, former Richmond Mayor were elected to public office. Prior to Prince\'s election black clergy made political endorsements and served as appointees to the Richmond School Board and other boards throughout the city. Today religion and politics continues to thrive in the Commonwealth of Virginia. The Honorable Dwight C. Jones, a prominent Baptist pastor and former Chairman of the Richmond School Board and Member of the Virginia House of Delegates serves as Mayor of the City of Richmond.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Richmond\'s government changed in 2004 from a\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Council-manager" title="Council-manager">\n        council-manager\n       </a>\n       form of government to an at-large, popularly elected Mayor. In a landslide election, incumbent mayor Rudy McCollum was defeated by\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/L._Douglas_Wilder" title="L. Douglas Wilder">\n        L. Douglas Wilder\n       </a>\n       , who previously served Virginia as the first elected African American governor in the United States since\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Reconstruction_era_of_the_United_States" title="Reconstruction era of the United States">\n        Reconstruction\n       </a>\n       . The current mayor of Richmond is\n       <a href="/wiki/Levar_Stoney" title="Levar Stoney">\n        Levar Stoney\n       </a>\n       who was elected in 2016.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-146">\n        <a href="#cite_note-146">\n         [143]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The mayor is not a part of the Richmond City Council.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       As of 2017\n       <sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;">\n        <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Richmond,_Virginia&amp;action=edit">\n         [update]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       , the Richmond City Council consisted of:\n      </p>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        Chris A. Hilbert, 3rd District (Northside), President of Council\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Cynthia I Newbille, 7th District (East End) Vice-President of Council\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Andreas D. Addison, 1st District (West End)\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Kimberly B. Gray, 2nd District (North Central)\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Kristen Nye Larson, 4th District (Southwest)\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Parker C. Agelasto, 5th District (Central)\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Ellen F. Robertson, 6th District (Gateway)\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Reva M. Trammell, 8th District (Southside)\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Michael J. Jones 9th District (South Central)\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <p>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-147">\n        <a href="#cite_note-147">\n         [144]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Education">\n        Education\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Richmond,_Virginia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Education">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tjhs.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1899" data-file-width="2820" height="148" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Tjhs.jpg/220px-Tjhs.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Tjhs.jpg/330px-Tjhs.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Tjhs.jpg/440px-Tjhs.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Tjhs.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         The\n         <a href="/wiki/Art_Deco" title="Art Deco">\n          Art Deco\n         </a>\n         -styled Thomas Jefferson High School in the near West End\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Richmond_Public_Schools" title="Richmond Public Schools">\n        Richmond Public Schools\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The city of Richmond operates 28 elementary schools, nine\n       <a href="/wiki/Middle_school" title="Middle school">\n        middle schools\n       </a>\n       , and eight high schools, serving a total student population of 24,000 students.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rps_facts_148-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-rps_facts-148">\n         [145]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       There is one Governor\'s School in the city \xe2\x88\x92 the\n       <a href="/wiki/Maggie_L._Walker_Governor%27s_School_for_Government_and_International_Studies" title="Maggie L. Walker Governor\'s School for Government and International Studies">\n        Maggie L. Walker Governor\'s School for Government and International Studies\n       </a>\n       . In 2008, it was named as one of\n       <a href="/wiki/Newsweek" title="Newsweek">\n        Newsweek\n       </a>\n       magazine\'s 18 "public elite" high schools,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hickey_Gordon_149-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Hickey_Gordon-149">\n         [146]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and in 2012, it was rated #16 of America\'s best high schools overall.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Newsweek_2012_150-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Newsweek_2012-150">\n         [147]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Richmond\'s public school district also runs one of Virginia\'s four public\n       <a href="/wiki/Charter_school" title="Charter school">\n        charter schools\n       </a>\n       , the Patrick Henry School of Science and Arts, which was founded in 2010.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-charter_schools_151-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-charter_schools-151">\n         [148]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       As of 2008, there were 36 private schools serving grades one or higher in the city of Richmond.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-private_schools_list_152-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-private_schools_list-152">\n         [149]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Some of these schools include:\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Benedictine_High_School_(Richmond,_Virginia)" title="Benedictine High School (Richmond, Virginia)">\n        Benedictine High School\n       </a>\n       , St. Bridget School,\n       <a href="/wiki/Brook_Road_Academy" title="Brook Road Academy">\n        Brook Road Academy\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Collegiate_School_(Richmond,_Virginia)" title="Collegiate School (Richmond, Virginia)">\n        Collegiate School\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/St._Christopher%27s_School,_Richmond" title="St. Christopher\'s School, Richmond">\n        St. Christopher\'s School\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Saint_Gertrude_High_School" title="Saint Gertrude High School">\n        St. Gertrude High School\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/St._Catherine%27s_School,_Richmond,_Virginia" title="St. Catherine\'s School, Richmond, Virginia">\n        St. Catherine\'s School\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Southside_Baptist_Christian_School" title="Southside Baptist Christian School">\n        Southside Baptist Christian School\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Northstar_Academy_(Richmond,_Virginia)" title="Northstar Academy (Richmond, Virginia)">\n        Northstar Academy\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Steward_School" title="The Steward School">\n        The Steward School\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Trinity_Episcopal_High_School" title="Trinity Episcopal High School">\n        Trinity Episcopal School\n       </a>\n       , and Veritas School.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Colleges_and_universities">\n        Colleges and universities\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Richmond,_Virginia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Colleges and universities">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       The Richmond area has many major institutions of higher education, including\n       <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Commonwealth_University" title="Virginia Commonwealth University">\n        Virginia Commonwealth University\n       </a>\n       (public),\n       <a href="/wiki/University_of_Richmond" title="University of Richmond">\n        University of Richmond\n       </a>\n       (private),\n       <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Union_University" title="Virginia Union University">\n        Virginia Union University\n       </a>\n       (private),\n       <a href="/wiki/Virginia_College" title="Virginia College">\n        Virginia College\n       </a>\n       (private),\n       <a href="/wiki/South_University" title="South University">\n        South University\n       </a>\n       \xe2\x80\x93Richmond (private, for-profit),\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-153">\n        <a href="#cite_note-153">\n         [150]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Union_Theological_Seminary_%26_Presbyterian_School_of_Christian_Education" title="Union Theological Seminary &amp; Presbyterian School of Christian Education">\n        Union Theological Seminary &amp; Presbyterian School of Christian Education\n       </a>\n       (private), and the Baptist Theological Seminary in Richmond (BTSR\xe2\x80\x94private). Several community colleges are found in the metro area, including\n       <a href="/wiki/J._Sargeant_Reynolds_Community_College" title="J. Sargeant Reynolds Community College">\n        J. Sargeant Reynolds Community College\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/John_Tyler_Community_College" title="John Tyler Community College">\n        John Tyler Community College\n       </a>\n       (\n       <a href="/wiki/Chesterfield_County,_Virginia" title="Chesterfield County, Virginia">\n        Chesterfield County\n       </a>\n       ). In addition, there are several Technical Colleges in Richmond including ITT Technical Institute,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ECPI_College_of_Technology" title="ECPI College of Technology">\n        ECPI College of Technology\n       </a>\n       and Centura College. There are several vocational colleges also, such as Fortis College and Bryant Stratton College.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/Virginia_State_University" title="Virginia State University">\n        Virginia State University\n       </a>\n       is located about 20 miles (32\xc2\xa0km) south of Richmond, in the suburb of\n       <a href="/wiki/Ettrick,_Virginia" title="Ettrick, Virginia">\n        Ettrick\n       </a>\n       , just outside\n       <a href="/wiki/Petersburg,_Virginia" title="Petersburg, Virginia">\n        Petersburg\n       </a>\n       .\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Randolph-Macon_College" title="Randolph-Macon College">\n        Randolph-Macon College\n       </a>\n       is located about 15 miles (24\xc2\xa0km) north of Richmond, in the incorporated town of\n       <a href="/wiki/Ashland,_Virginia" title="Ashland, Virginia">\n        Ashland\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Infrastructure">\n        Infrastructure\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Richmond,_Virginia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Infrastructure">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Transportation">\n        Transportation\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Richmond,_Virginia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Transportation">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Main_Street_Station.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1504" data-file-width="1000" height="331" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Main_Street_Station.jpg/220px-Main_Street_Station.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Main_Street_Station.jpg/330px-Main_Street_Station.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Main_Street_Station.jpg/440px-Main_Street_Station.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Main_Street_Station.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Richmond\'s downtown\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Main_Street_Station_(Richmond)" title="Main Street Station (Richmond)">\n          Main Street Station\n         </a>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Transportation_in_Richmond,_Virginia" title="Transportation in Richmond, Virginia">\n        Transportation in Richmond, Virginia\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The Greater Richmond area is served by the\n       <a href="/wiki/Richmond_International_Airport" title="Richmond International Airport">\n        Richmond International Airport\n       </a>\n       (\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/International_Air_Transport_Association_airport_code" title="International Air Transport Association airport code">\n        IATA\n       </a>\n       :\n       <b>\n        RIC\n       </b>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/International_Civil_Aviation_Organization_airport_code" title="International Civil Aviation Organization airport code">\n        ICAO\n       </a>\n       :\n       <b>\n        KRIC\n       </b>\n       ), located in nearby\n       <a href="/wiki/Sandston,_Virginia" title="Sandston, Virginia">\n        Sandston\n       </a>\n       , seven miles (11\xc2\xa0km) southeast of Richmond and within an hour drive of historic\n       <a href="/wiki/Williamsburg,_Virginia" title="Williamsburg, Virginia">\n        Williamsburg, Virginia\n       </a>\n       . Richmond International is now served by nine airlines with over 200 daily flights providing non-stop service to major destination markets and connecting flights to destinations worldwide. A record 3.3 million passengers used Richmond International Airport in 2006, a 13% increase over 2005.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Richmond is a major hub for intercity\n       <a href="/wiki/Bus" title="Bus">\n        bus\n       </a>\n       company\n       <a href="/wiki/Greyhound_Lines" title="Greyhound Lines">\n        Greyhound Lines\n       </a>\n       , with its terminal at 2910 N Boulevard. Multiple runs per day connect directly with Washington, D.C., New York, Raleigh, and elsewhere. Direct trips to New York take approximately 7.5 hours. Discount carrier\n       <a href="/wiki/Megabus_(North_America)" title="Megabus (North America)">\n        Megabus\n       </a>\n       also provides curbside service from outside of Main Street Station, with fares starting at $1. Direct service is available to Washington, D.C.,\n       <a href="/wiki/Hampton_Roads" title="Hampton Roads">\n        Hampton Roads\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Charlotte" title="Charlotte">\n        Charlotte\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Raleigh,_North_Carolina" title="Raleigh, North Carolina">\n        Raleigh\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Baltimore" title="Baltimore">\n        Baltimore\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia" title="Philadelphia">\n        Philadelphia\n       </a>\n       . Most other connections to Megabus served cities, such as New York, can be made from Washington, D.C.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-154">\n        <a href="#cite_note-154">\n         [151]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Richmond, and the surrounding metropolitan area, was granted a roughly $25 million grant from the U.S. Department of Transportation in 2014\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-155">\n        <a href="#cite_note-155">\n         [152]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       to support the\n       <a href="/wiki/GRTC_Pulse" title="GRTC Pulse">\n        GRTC Pulse\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/Bus_rapid_transit" title="Bus rapid transit">\n        bus rapid transit\n       </a>\n       system, which will run along Broad Street from Willow Lawn to Rocketts Landing, in the first phase of an improved public transportation hub for the region.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Local\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Transit_(transportation)" title="Transit (transportation)">\n        transit\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Paratransit" title="Paratransit">\n        paratransit\n       </a>\n       bus service in Richmond,\n       <a href="/wiki/Henrico_County,_Virginia" title="Henrico County, Virginia">\n        Henrico\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Chesterfield_County,_Virginia" title="Chesterfield County, Virginia">\n        Chesterfield\n       </a>\n       counties is provided by the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Greater_Richmond_Transit_of_Richmond,_Virginia" title="Greater Richmond Transit of Richmond, Virginia">\n        Greater Richmond Transit Company\n       </a>\n       (GRTC). The GRTC, however, serves only small parts of the suburban counties. The far West End (Innsbrook and Short Pump) and almost all of Chesterfield County have no public transportation despite dense housing, retail, and office development. According to a 2008 GRTC operations analysis report, a majority of GRTC riders utilize their services because they do not have an available alternative such as a private vehicle.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GRTC_rider_stats_156-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-GRTC_rider_stats-156">\n         [153]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The Richmond area also has two railroad stations served by\n       <a href="/wiki/Amtrak" title="Amtrak">\n        Amtrak\n       </a>\n       . Each station receives regular service from north of Richmond including Washington, D.C., Philadelphia, and New York. The suburban\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Richmond_Staples_Mill_Road_(Amtrak_station)" title="Richmond Staples Mill Road (Amtrak station)">\n        Staples Mill Road Station\n       </a>\n       is located on a major north-south freight line and receives all service to and from all points south including,\n       <a href="/wiki/Raleigh,_North_Carolina" title="Raleigh, North Carolina">\n        Raleigh\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Durham,_North_Carolina" title="Durham, North Carolina">\n        Durham\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Savannah,_Georgia" title="Savannah, Georgia">\n        Savannah\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Newport_News,_Virginia" title="Newport News, Virginia">\n        Newport News\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Williamsburg,_Virginia" title="Williamsburg, Virginia">\n        Williamsburg\n       </a>\n       and Florida. Richmond\'s only railway station located within the city limits, the historic\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Main_Street_Station_(Richmond)" title="Main Street Station (Richmond)">\n        Main Street Station\n       </a>\n       , was renovated in 2004.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-157">\n        <a href="#cite_note-157">\n         [154]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       As of 2010, the station only receives trains headed to and from\n       <a href="/wiki/Newport_News,_Virginia" title="Newport News, Virginia">\n        Newport News\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Williamsburg,_Virginia" title="Williamsburg, Virginia">\n        Williamsburg\n       </a>\n       due to track layout. As a result, the Staples Mill Road station receives more trains and serves more passengers overall.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Richmond also benefits from an excellent position in reference to the state\'s transportation network, lying at the junction of east-west\n       <a href="/wiki/Interstate_64" title="Interstate 64">\n        Interstate 64\n       </a>\n       and north-south\n       <a href="/wiki/Interstate_95_in_Virginia" title="Interstate 95 in Virginia">\n        Interstate 95\n       </a>\n       , two of the most heavily traveled highways in the state, as well as along several major rail lines.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Major_highways">\n        Major highways\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span href="/wiki/Virginia_State_Route_353" title="Virginia State Route 353">\n           SR\xc2\xa0353\n          </a>\n         </span>\n        </li>\n       </ul>\n      </div>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Utilities">\n        Utilities\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Richmond,_Virginia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Utilities">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/Electric_power" title="Electric power">\n        Electricity\n       </a>\n       in the Richmond Metro area is provided by\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dominion_Virginia_Power" title="Dominion Virginia Power">\n        Dominion Virginia Power\n       </a>\n       . The company, based in Richmond, is one of the nation\'s largest producers of energy, serving retail energy customers in nine states. Electricity is provided in the Richmond area primarily by the\n       <a href="/wiki/North_Anna_Nuclear_Generating_Station" title="North Anna Nuclear Generating Station">\n        North Anna Nuclear Generating Station\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Surry_Nuclear_Generating_Station" title="Surry Nuclear Generating Station">\n        Surry Nuclear Generating Station\n       </a>\n       , as well as a coal-fired station in\n       <a href="/wiki/Chester,_Virginia" title="Chester, Virginia">\n        Chester, Virginia\n       </a>\n       . These three plants provide a total of 4,453\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Megawatts" title="Megawatts">\n        megawatts\n       </a>\n       of power. Several other natural gas plants provide extra power during times of peak demand. These include facilities in\n       <a href="/wiki/Chester,_Virginia" title="Chester, Virginia">\n        Chester\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Surry,_Virginia" title="Surry, Virginia">\n        Surry\n       </a>\n       , and two plants in Richmond (Gravel Neck and Darbytown).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-158">\n        <a href="#cite_note-158">\n         [155]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Natural gas in the Richmond Metro area is provided by the city\'s Department of Public Utilities and also serves portions of\n       <a href="/wiki/Henrico_County,_Virginia" title="Henrico County, Virginia">\n        Henrico\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Chesterfield_County,_Virginia" title="Chesterfield County, Virginia">\n        Chesterfield\n       </a>\n       counties.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Water is provided by the city\'s Department of Public Utilities, and is one of the largest water producers in Virginia, with a modern plant that can treat up to 132 million gallons of water a day from the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/James_River_(Virginia)" title="James River (Virginia)">\n        James River\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-159">\n        <a href="#cite_note-159">\n         [156]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The facility also provides water to the surrounding area through wholesale contracts with\n       <a href="/wiki/Henrico_County,_Virginia" title="Henrico County, Virginia">\n        Henrico\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Chesterfield_County,_Virginia" title="Chesterfield County, Virginia">\n        Chesterfield\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Hanover_County,_Virginia" title="Hanover County, Virginia">\n        Hanover\n       </a>\n       counties. Overall, this results in a facility that provides water for approximately 500,000 people.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/Wastewater" title="Wastewater">\n        wastewater\n       </a>\n       treatment plant and distribution system of water mains, pumping stations and storage facilities provide water to approximately 62,000 customers in the city. There is also a wastewater treatment plant located on the south bank of the James River. This plant can treat up to 70 million gallons of water per day of sanitary sewage and stormwater before returning it to the river. The wastewater utility also operates and maintains 1,500 miles (2,400\xc2\xa0km) of sanitary sewer and pumping stations, 38 miles (61\xc2\xa0km) of intercepting sewer lines, and the Shockoe Retention Basin, a 44-million-gallon stormwater reservoir used during heavy rains.\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="International_relations">\n        International relations\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Sister_cities">\n        Sister cities\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n
